Krasnicki (@Solofunk) and Alice Hou (@Fbitach). 
Base 
In 2025, Base cemented itself as the leading L2 across a range of metrics. Few, however, illustrate its dominance over the L2 ecosystem as clearly 
as revenue. 
 
While L2 chain revenues have declined signiﬁcantly from their 2024 peak, Base has continued to capture an outsized share over the L2 market. In 
December 2023, Base generated $2.5 million in chain revenue, just 5% of total L2 revenue of $53.7 million. One year later, Base’s chain revenue 
rose to $14.7 million, accounting for 63% of the $23.5 million generated by all L2s in December 2024. This trend has persisted into 2025. 
Year-to-date, Base has generated $75.4 million in chain revenue, representing 62% of the $120.7 million in total L2 chain revenue. 
               
 


---

## Page 108

107 
 
Base’s lead is not conﬁned to revenue, which can favor high-velocity transactions that are easier to monetize at the chain level. Base also became 
the leading L2 by DeFi TVL after ﬂipping Arbitrum One in January 2025. Today, Base’s $4.36 billion in DeFi TVL represents 46% of total L2 
DeFi TVL. Perhaps most importantly, Base’s share of DeFi TVL has steadily increased throughout 2025, rising from 33% at the beginning of the 
year. 
Base’s biggest advantage over other L2s is distribution, and it’s hard to overstate how meaningful that is. Per Coinbase’s latest 10-Q, the CEX had 
9.3 million monthly transacting users in Q3, giving Base direct access to a massive, already onboarded user base that other L2s simply cannot 
match. While most L2s must acquire users through incentives or third-party integrations, Base beneﬁts from native distribution through the largest 
American CEX. 
               
 


---

## Page 109

108 
 
Base has also distinguished itself as an environment where applications can scale into meaningful businesses. Year-to-date, applications on Base 
have generated $369.9 million in revenue. Notably, application revenue is concentrated in Aerodrome, which accounts for 43% of total application 
revenue at $160.5 million. However, Base’s premier DEX is not the only application to ﬁnd success in 2025. 
The AI agent launchpad Virtuals has generated $43.2 million in revenue, representing 12% of Base’s application revenue, while the recently 
launched sports prediction app Football.Fun has generated $4.7 million. Together, these applications point to a healthy cohort of 
revenue-generating products across multiple sectors, rather than Base’s activity being driven by a single application or use case. 
               
 


---

## Page 110

109 
 
The scale of this distribution advantage is best exempliﬁed through Coinbase’s partnership with Morpho, which allows Coinbase users to take out 
USDC loans against their crypto holdings directly on the platform. While the user experience lives inside Coinbase, the collateral and loan 
execution occur onchain via Morpho’s deployment on Base. Despite being live for less than a year, the product has already seen signiﬁcant 
adoption. 
Coinbase users have originated $866.3 million in loans through the partnership, which now accounts for 90% of active loans on Morpho’s Base 
deployment. Over the same period, Morpho’s Base TVL has increased 1,906% year-to-date, rising from $48.2 million to $966.4 million. Base’s 
distribution advantage means onchain activity can show up as a byproduct of product usage on Coinbase. This onboarding route is unavailable to 
other L2s, leaving them largely dependent on incentive programs to pull liquidity and users into their DeFi ecosystems. 
               
 


---

## Page 111

110 
 
Even as Base’s DeFi TVL has grown throughout 2025 and revenue has held steady, user behavior onchain has begun to change. USDC is now the 
top application on Base by daily average ﬁltered users (unique addresses with at least two transactions and more than 0.0001 in gas spent on a 
given contract) with 83,400 users in November. That ﬁgure is up 233% year-over-year from 25,100. 
At the same time, retail interaction with DEXs has declined sharply. Daily average ﬁltered users on Uniswap and Aerodrome are down 74% and 
49%, respectively. More interestingly, DEX volumes on Base reached all-time highs in 2025, meaning that activity on Uniswap and Aerodrome is 
increasingly concentrated among larger, higher-volume traders. 
Base’s Big Bet in 2026: The Base App 
Base’s proximity to Coinbase gives it a luxury that few chains really have. It has already built a meaningful moat in users, liquidity, and 
applications. Base leads all L2s in chain revenue, has the deepest DeFi TVL in the category, and beneﬁts from a steady stream of users coming 
onchain through Coinbase. In other words, Base is not ﬁghting for relevance or traction in the way most L2s still are. 
With this moat established, Base is now looking beyond the core L2 metrics and toward the creator economy. An opportunity that, if captured, 
               
 


---

## Page 112

111 
represents nearly half a trillion dollars in total addressable market. At the center of Base’s go-to-market strategy for this direction is the Base App, 
an “everything app” that aims to bring together custody, trading, social, and other core wallet functions all in one place. Unlike most crypto 
wallets, the Base app includes several features that push beyond basic asset management: 
● A social feed powered by Farcaster and Zora. 
● Direct messaging and group chats via XMTP, including interactions with other users and AI agents such as Bankr. 
● Mini-app discovery, allowing users to access and interact with mini-apps directly within the Base app. 
 
The Base app launched in private beta in July, with access initially limited to a waitlisted, invite-only group of users. Even so, the Base app has 
seen meaningful growth. In total, 148,400 users have created an account, with signups accelerating in November, increasing 93% MoM. Retention 
also appears strong, with weekly active users at 6,300 (up 74% MoM) and monthly active users at 10,500 (up 7% MoM). Although not explicitly 
conﬁrmed, it’s likely that the Base app will exit private beta this month, setting the stage for the app to be publicly available to anyone before the 
new year. 
               
 


---

## Page 113

112 
 
The most important facet of the onchain economy Base is trying to build is enabling creators to earn directly from the content they produce. 
Content created on the Base app is tokenized by default (though users can opt out), turning each post into a tradable market. Creators earn a 
portion of the trading fees generated by their content, 1% of each trade. 
Looking ahead, users will also be able to launch creator coins for their accounts directly within the Base app, adding another monetization avenue 
(the feature is currently in early access). Under the hood, both creator and content coins are tokenized via Zora. To date, creators have collectively 
earned $6.1 million through Zora’s tokenization model, averaging $1.1 million in monthly payouts since July. 
               
 


---

## Page 114

113 
 
In total, more than 6.52 million creator and content coins have been tokenized through Zora. Of those, 6.45 million (roughly 99%) failed to reach 
ﬁve trades. Only 17,800 coins, or 0.3% of the total, continued to be traded more than 48 hours after launch. 
Before reading too much into this, it’s worth noting that the vast majority of content posted on the internet is eﬀectively valueless. In that context, 
99% of coins failing to gain traction may simply reﬂect a natural distribution of online content rather than a structural ﬂaw in Base’s approach. 
The coins that survive beyond 48 hours are the ones that matter. In our view, a creator or content coin trading beyond that window is a strong 
indicator that either the creator or the content was genuinely valuable. 
Put diﬀerently, Base has barely made a dent in the creator economy so far. Only 17,800 creator and content coins have shown sustained activity, 
which is a rounding error relative to the scale of online content produced every day. Pessimists might look at this and conclude that the model 
simply isn’t working. Optimists, however, would argue the opposite. Base’s penetration into the creator economy is eﬀectively zero, which leaves 
a massive surface area for growth if distribution, discovery, and tooling improve (perhaps from the public launch of the Base App?). Regardless, 
increasing the number of coins that reach a lifespan beyond 48 hours should be a main focus for Base in 2026. 
               
 


---

## Page 115

114 
Lastly, Base also has what may be the most potent incentive mechanism left in crypto: a token. In September, Base conﬁrmed that it is exploring a 
network token, though no concrete details around distribution, utility, or a potential launch date have been disclosed. What makes a potential 
BASE token particularly interesting is not the token itself, but how it could be used. Unlike most L2s, Base does not need a token to bootstrap 
liquidity or activity at the chain level. Instead, a token could be used much more selectively to incentivize participation in the onchain creator 
economy, rewarding behaviors that drive durable user engagement, content creation, and social activity, rather than short-term transactional 
metrics. 
Taken together, with the core L2 already established, Base is using its distribution, product surface area, and potential token incentives to push 
further up the stack and experiment with consumer and creator-native use cases at scale. If this works, Base ends up building a moat around social 
and creator behavior, one that is far stickier than DeFi TVL or stablecoin balances, and one that other L2s are largely not even attempting to 
compete on. 
MegaETH 
As explored in our report, Next-gen Chains: Strategic Diﬀerentiation, MegaETH is a much anticipated L2 making unapologetic tradeoﬀs within 
the blockchain trilemma to achieve extreme optimization toward scalability and enable the ﬁrst “real-time blockchain.” Testnet went live in March 
with many claiming MegaETH’s performance could be a step function improvement not only in the L2 sector, but for blockchains broadly. 
               
 


---

## Page 116

115 
 
MegaETH will feature 10 millisecond “mini-blocks” while aiming for up to 100,000 TPS. The high-level infrastructure is not radically diﬀerent 
from L2s like those powered by Arbitrum Nitro or the OP Stack. MegaETH’s performance improvements stem from network-level optimizations, 
the hardware required to run a sequencer, and the specialization of four node types that allow for an exponential increase in gas limits. 
MegaETH’s sequencer will be powerful enough to produce mini-blocks that update the network’s state while providing transaction inclusion 
guarantees for users and applications, allowing them to operate at an extremely rapid, real-time pace. The project team has curated two cohorts of 
ecosystem projects, which together, are dubbed the “MegaMaﬁa.” The MegaMaﬁa aims to take advantage of MegaETH’s performance to create 
novel applications and experiences that are only on MegaETH (OMEGA). Additionally, MegaETH’s USDm native stablecoin being integrated 
across MegaMaﬁa apps should bootstrap initial revenue generation for the network, with the opportunity to scale to something greater long-term. 
Another unique approach taken by MegaETH is in its token design. MegaETH’s rotating sequencer set will be enabled by the MEGA token, 
which will be required to be staked in order to operate a sequencer. MEGA will also be staked for the ability to bid on priority transaction 
inclusion, likely from entities needing low latency like market makers and MegaMaﬁa apps. These two use cases are novel for an L2 token, and 
could be in demand if MegaETH successfully fosters high-velocity trading activity that breeds REV. If MEGA performs well in 2026, it could 
               
 


---

## Page 117

116 
push the market to demand increased utility from pre-existing L2 tokens whose primary uses are governance and incentives. 
MegaETH has also made a concerted eﬀort to align a large base of early stakeholders with skin in the game, having allocated more MEGA to 
individual investors than to venture capital ﬁrms. Many tokens have been scrutinized for launching at a low ﬂoat, high fully diluted valuation, with 
large portions of token supply controlled by insiders. MegaETH’s approach aims for a diﬀerent outcome. Earlier rounds like the $10 million 
community sale or the mint of “The Fluﬄe” NFT came at favorable valuations. The ﬁnal round occurred this October in a public ICO that raised 
$50 million from over 5,000 investors on Echo for 5% of MEGA. MegaETH has expanded the pool of “insiders” to include individual believers 
and core community members. 
MegaETH is built diﬀerent. Not only architecturally, but also in its ecosystem and token design. These approaches could result in net-new 
primitives with adoption bootstrapped by early power users with skin in the game. Furthermore, upon the token’s launch, token inﬂation and 
vesting will be uniquely tied to performance KPIs rather than dates, with rewards being limited to stakers of the MEGA token. 
Beta mainnet just launched in early-access for builders in December. Early network activity, ecosystem growth, and token performance, all have 
the potential to exceed expectations because of MegaETH’s unique strategies. MegaETH is one to watch as the new L2 on the block that has a 
realistic shot at becoming a leading rollup by revenue in 2026. 
Mantle 
In 2025, Mantle successfully pivoted its narrative from a general-purpose L2 into a comprehensive institutional ﬁnancial crypto infrastructure. The 
majority of the protocol’s growth was spent repositioning itself away from the saturated ETH L2 category and toward a more deﬁned role as 
infrastructure for institutional onchain ﬁnance. 
Many L2s competed for retail traction throughout the year. Mantle diﬀerentiated by honing in on its vertically integrated ﬁnancial stack, using its 
rich treasury and exchange partnerships to accelerate deployment. 
What Went Right in 2025 
               
 


---

## Page 118

117 
 
MNT was the top-performing L2 token by market capitalization in 2025, standing out in a year where the broader L2 sector performed poortly. 
The token’s circulating market cap was the 3rd-largest amongst L2s at the start of 2024, but was 1st throughout 2025, remaining around the 30th 
spot throughout the year. 
Mantle’s performance in 2025 was closely tied to its exchange-aligned model through Bybit. Deep integration with Bybit (where MNT is now 
used for trading pairs, fee discounts, and VIP collateral) supported MNT’s rise to the top-ranked L2 by market capitalization by the end of 2025. 
This approach mirrors the structure of other highly active networks, including Base and BNB Chain, both of which maintain close operational and 
liquidity ties to centralized exchanges such as Coinbase and Binance. In this context, Mantle’s integration with Bybit functions as an eﬀective 
mechanism for attracting users, liquidity, and asset integrations. 
Another deﬁning move in 2025 was establishing a use case separate from the broader L2 cohort. The “banking chain” framing allowed the 
network to attract institutionally-oriented projects and anchor its valuation through periods of weak sentiment in the L2 category. 
Mantle also allocated DAO capital toward building an institutional-grade liquidity layer. This included mETH, a liquid staking asset, and cmETH, 
a restaking derivative, which collectively attracted over $1.07 billion in capital. In addition, the MI4 index fund, a tokenized portfolio designed for 
               
 


---

## Page 119

118 
crypto-native beta exposure, managed $173 million by the end of 2025. These products formed the foundation of Mantle’s structured yield 
strategy. 
In Q3, Mantle moved to an OP-Succinct ZK Validium architecture, reducing withdrawal ﬁnality to approximately six hours. It also integrated 
EigenDA to bring down data availability costs. This adjustment prioritized performance characteristics that align with institutional use cases, 
including lower transaction costs and predictable settlement times. 
2026 Outlook 
Mantle enters 2026 with multiple initiatives in motion. Its success will depend on execution across both institutional and consumer distribution 
channels. 
Launched in mid-2025, the UR mobile application serves as a front-end banking layer for crypto services. UR simpliﬁes the DeFi stack and aims 
to onboard users directly from Bybit into onchain activity. If it converts a fraction of that funnel, Mantle could establish a replicable path to retail 
distribution that most L2s have struggled to secure. 
Mantle’s TaaS (Tokenization-as-a-service) platform began with early deployments from Ondo (USDY) and World Liberty Financial (WLFI). 
Success in 2026 depends on Mantle attracting additional asset originators and gaining adoption among allocators that need fast, compliant 
settlement infrastructure for yield-bearing instruments. 
The key question for 2026 is whether Mantle can support broader development and usage beyond its exchange funnel. If native primitives like 
mETH and FBTC maintain user retention without additional incentives, and if developers deploy outside of grant programs, Mantle positions 
itself to sustain its institutional role. 
ZKsync 
2025 was a year of intense technical execution, transforming the ZK Stack into what Matter Labs calls “the Bank Stack of Ethereum,” an 
infrastructure that can bring institutions onchain with privacy, scalability, and compliance. The broader market also rediscovered privacy, with 
renewed interest in ZK-based systems, and ZKsync’s answer is to oﬀer Prividiums, private chains secured by ZK proofs rather than isolated 
permissioned ledgers. 
               
 


---

## Page 120

119 
 
Airbender is ZKsync’s next-generation RISC-V proof system, purpose-built to generate eﬃcient ZK proofs of RISC-V bytecode execution. It is 
built on highly optimized STARK/FRI implementations and is designed to be fast, cheap, and ﬂexible across a wide range of use cases without 
compromising security. On a single NVIDIA H100 GPU, Airbender achieves roughly 21.8 MHz of eﬀective throughput and can process an 
average Ethereum block in about 17 seconds pre-recursion and around 35 seconds end-to-end, which is signiﬁcantly faster than comparable 
open-source zkVMs. Airbender runs on consumer GPUs and standard hardware rather than large datacenters, making it realistic for institutions to 
run proving inside their own environments while still keeping proof-to-settlement windows tight enough for real ﬁnancial workﬂows. 
The Atlas upgrade took proving gains made possible by Airbender and targeted the full settlement loop rather than just “more TPS.” By pairing 
ZKsync OS with Airbender, the Atlas upgrade enabled 15,000+ TPS, ~1 second ZK ﬁnality, and ~$0.0001 a proving cost per transfer. Atlas also 
restructured the stack so the sequencer focuses on low-latency ordering while asynchronous components handle proving and posting 
commitments, and it introduced interop and messaging upgrades that cut coordination latency across chains. 
With Atlas compressing proof-to-settlement timelines and lowering proving costs, ZKsync used 2025 to expand from pure L2 scaling into an 
enterprise strategy built around Prividiums, giving institutions a path onto crypto rails without forcing them into fully public infrastructure. 
               
 


---

## Page 121

120 
Prividums have seen early traction with partners like Memento and Deutsche Bank. Each Prividium is a permissioned validium chain that runs in 
an institution’s own environment and keeps balances and transaction data private while anchoring to Ethereum through ZK proofs. The 
permissioning system and selective disclosure modules enable operators to deﬁne who can view what, while regulators or auditors can verify 
compliance without gaining full visibility into the ledger. With Interop, Prividiums can tap Ethereum liquidity directly: assets move to aliased 
accounts on mainnet, interact with protocols like Aave, and can be bridged back, all while preserving identity and permissions. This is the ﬁrst 
architecture that enables institutions to maintain private systems while still accessing Ethereum’s liquidity. 
In 2026, ZKsync plans to deprecate ZKsync Lite, the original 1.0 rollup that served as a proof of concept for production ZK systems. Lite’s sunset 
is a clear signal that in 2026, Matter Labs will be fully focused on extending the ZK Stack through the ZKsync Era as the main public hub, with 
the addition of new ZKsync OS-based chains, Prividiums for institutions, and the ZKsync Gateway as the shared coordination layer for the Elastic 
Network. 
Against that backdrop, success in 2026 is less about shipping new primitives and more about proving that this stack can carry real institutional 
workloads at scale. In practical terms, three outcomes stand out. 
Achieve PMF with Prividiums 
The ﬁrst success condition is turning early traction with Memento and Deutsche Bank into repeatable product-market ﬁt. That means onboarding 
more banks, ﬁntechs, and enterprises that run Prividiums as core infrastructure for intraday repo, cross-border payments, and internal treasury 
systems. The long-term vision is that every serious business operates its own Prividium, just as it maintains a corporate bank account today, with 
regulators using selective disclosure for oversight. Ideally, these chains will operate with interoperability enabled, allowing funds and messages to 
ﬂow seamlessly through Ethereum and other ZKsync chains, rather than remaining isolated private ledgers. 
Prove ZK Chains can “Skip the Cold Start” 
On the liquidity side, ZKsync now needs to demonstrate that “skip the cold start” is more than a slogan, which depends on ZK Chains fully 
enabling interoperability and actually driving users to tap into Ethereum liquidity. With Interop, ZK Chains and Prividiums can tap directly into 
Ethereum DeFi and transact against deep L1 liquidity using aliased accounts, without requiring isolated liquidity or custom integrations. This 
turns Ethereum into the liquidity backend for every ZK Chain, allowing actions like depositing into Aave or borrowing GHO to occur as seamless 
extensions of L2 workﬂows. The real test is whether users consistently route these ﬂows through ZK Chains. If Matter Labs can show that new 
chains launch with instant access and real usage of Ethereum liquidity, “skip the cold start” becomes a proven liquidity model rather than a 
marketing claim, and positions the ZK Stack as the ﬁrst architecture that marries private execution with public-market liquidity. 
Implement the ZK Token Flywheel 
               
 


---

## Page 122

121 
 
In 2026, success for ZKsync on the token side means implementing the proposed ZK token ﬂywheel for value accrual to the ZK token. 
Speciﬁcally, interoperability fees from cross-chain messaging and asset ﬂows, as well as licensing revenue from enterprise modules, need to be 
routed through the buy-and-allocate mechanism and used to purchase ZK on the market. Proceeds are designed to be allocated to burns, staking 
rewards, ecosystem incentives, and the treasury. 
Strategically, ZKsync enters 2026 with a diﬀerentiated position in the Ethereum L2 landscape as the ZKsync vision has developed beyond a single 
L2 to scale Ethereum into a network of interconnected ZK Chains for public and private access. ZKsync Era oﬀers EVM equivalent developer and 
user experience, ZKsync Gateway aggregates proofs and messages for cheaper and more interoperable settlement, Airbender and ZKsync OS 
provide a high-performance proving and execution stack, and Prividiums answer institutional requirements for privacy, compliance, and control 
while still relying on Ethereum’s incorruptibility, hard ﬁnality, and global liquidity. If Matter Labs can scale institutional adoption, drive 
meaningful ﬂows through interop and Gateway, and operationalize the ZK value ﬂywheel, ZKsync and the ZK Stack will be well placed to 
become the bank layer of Ethereum rather than just another generalized rollup. 
               
 


---

## Page 123

122 
To stay up to date with ZKsync and the Elastic Network, refer to Messari’s reports written by Hayden Booms (@0xBoomz). 
Solana 
Author: Matthew Nay 
 
Solana’s year started with the now infamous TRUMP launch, where the network proved it could handle more than $36 billion in volume over a 
24-hour period, and SOL hit an all-time high of $295. With such an explosion of activity to start the year, the ecosystem had high hopes for the 
remainder of 2025. 
The year, however, turned out to be up-and-down. Similar to many tokens, SOL faced multiple 50% drawdowns, struggled to overcome being the 
“Memecoin Chain” moniker, and saw the year’s biggest narratives develop winners elsewhere, perps on Hyperliquid, payments on stablechains, 
and the institutional interest on Ethereum. 
               
 


---

## Page 124

123 
Despite this, SOL maintained its spot in the top 10 assets for the entire year, saw its stablecoin supply triple, six ETFs launched, and the network 
received a commitment from Western Union to develop its stablecoin on the chain. Despite many considering 2025 to be a down year for Solana 
compared to 2024, several key metrics, including REV, transactions, and spot volume, all indicate that Solana remains among the leading 
general-purpose L1s. 
Spot DEX Dominance 
 
Solana continued its lead in spot DEX volume this year, with $4.2 billion in volume over the last three months, resulting in a 30% market share. 
At the beginning of the year, this was primarily driven by memecoin volume but later shifted with over 50% of all volume stemming from 
SOL-Stablecoin pairs by November. We expect this trend to continue in 2026, along with an increase in non-SOL majors being traded on the 
chain. 
               
 


---

## Page 125

124 
 
Solana DEX volume had the greatest start to a year any chain had ever seen. During the TRUMP launch, DEXs handled over $36 billion in 
volume, equivalent to roughly 10% of the daily volume on the NASDAQ. Shortly thereafter, volumes fell rapidly due to a decline in memecoin 
volume and the broader market selloﬀ in April. Since then, there has been a steady increase in DEX volume mainly driven by the emergence of 
prop AMMs, like HumidiFi and Tessera. 
               
 


---

## Page 126

125 
 
Prop AMMs, short for proprietary AMMs, saw their ﬁrst iteration with Liﬁnity in 2022, but didn’t start to take oﬀ until 2024 with the launch of 
SolFi by the Ellipsis team. In 2025, volume share from prop AMMs increased from 10% to 50%, with the majority of the volume coming from the 
SOL-USDC pair. There are now seven major prop AMMs on Solana, with Humidiﬁ being the most dominant. Prop AMMs have an inherent 
advantage over traditional AMMs due to their architecture and the dominance of DEX aggregators on Solana. 
The biggest diﬀerence between prop AMMs and traditional AMMs is how liquidity is managed. Instead of holding passive LP positions, prop 
AMMs actively manage their own quotes, with no outside capital (hence its proprietary name). Most prop AMMs don’t have frontends and solely 
rely on order ﬂow from Jupiter, DFlow, or Titan. When a user requests a trade on an aggregator, each liquidity source on the chain competes to 
oﬀer the best price for that swap. 
This is where the prop AMMs truly shine, as each can utilize oracle updates to provide users with the best prices. On Solana, oracle updates are 
cheap from a compute perspective, especially compared to a swap, and because of how blocks are ordered in Jito auctions, these oracle updates 
land at the beginning of the block and provide users with the most up-to-date information. This also allows prop AMMs to be resistant to toxic 
ﬂows, as they have a pseudo-cancel priority and no public order book to trade against. 
               
 


---

## Page 127

126 
 
One of the most exciting developments coming from the prop AMM evolution is that it is bringing price discovery onchain for major assets. 
Historically, all price discovery has occurred on Binance, as the majority of majors volume takes place there. In 2025, HumidiFi did more volume 
on the SOL-USDC pair than all of Binance’s SOL-USD pairs 27 times, and SolFi was able to accomplish this four times. When you combine this 
feat with the fact that prop AMMs helped facilitate price discovery for ORE, and in total, Solana would’ve been the 5th or 6th largest venue to 
trade MON on launch, we expect Solana to lead in facilitating onchain price discovery for SOL once again next year. Solana will be the best place 
to trade SOL, even large orders, and at times it should lead price discovery for new token launches through Wormhole’s new Sunrise product, an 
application that enables assets from other ecosystems to be listed for day one trading on Solana. 
Resurgence of Solana Perp DEXs 
               
 


---

## Page 128

127 
 
Solana has had all-time highs in perp DEX volume over the last three months. However, the ecosystem is still losing to competitors like 
Hyperliquid, Aster, and Lighter. Next year, Solana’s perp DEXs should close that gap, and could even introduce innovative architectures to the 
perp DEX sector. There are four diﬀerent approaches being taken that all have a shot at winning the Solana market and competing with the 
sector’s market leaders: 
● Drift + Jito BAM: Drift has been the go-to platform for many Solana-native leverage traders, but has primarily been used for trading 
longer-tail assets. Jupiter Perps has historically dominated volume, oﬀering only BTC, ETH, and SOL. However, with the launch of Jito 
BAM, Drift can introduce maker priority cancels (a big diﬀerentiator for Hyperliquid) through BAM plugins. Drift is also expected to gain 
from Solana network improvements such as Alpenglow, increased block sizes, and further adoption of Firedancer, which launched in 
October. 
● Bullet: Formerly Zeta Markets, Bullet has spent 2025 redesigning their architecture to become a network extension on Solana. Bullet 
utilizes Solana for settlement and Celestia for data availability, enabling sub-1 millisecond latency on testnet. Bullet’s private mainnet went 
live on December 11 at Solana Breakpoint. 
● Bulk: Bulk is introducing a sidecar implementation for Solana perps by forking the Jito-Agave client, enabling validators to run 
               
 


---

## Page 129

128 
Bulk-Agave. Users’ positions remain on mainnet, but matching occurs through Bulk Tile, which runs on every validator node running 
Bulk-Agave. This architecture separates the order propagation and matching from onchain settlement, allowing for low latency and 
propagation times. Bulk has also stated that they will share 12.5% of revenue with validators running their client. 
● Phoenix Perps: Ellipsis Labs, the team behind Phoenix Spot and SolFi, is now pursuing Phoenix Perps. This implementation is the most 
experimental, as it uses prop AMMs as the liquidity source for its perp DEX. Phoenix Perps plans to bring the beneﬁts of prop AMMs, 
including tighter spreads, deeper books, and more adaptable quoting, to the perp space. Phoenix Perps launched in private beta at Solana 
Breakpoint. 
The perp DEX space on Solana is wide open and has multiple teams capable of competing with market leaders. 2026 will be the year when this 
gap is closed. 
Onchain Capital Formation 
Another Solana sector that we expect to grow in 2026, is onchain capital formation. What pump.fun started as launchpads for memecoins, has 
expanded into launchpads for tokens attached to relevant projects. Currently there are three options for teams launching tokens on Solana that do 
not want to go through a memecoin launchpad: 
● Metaplex Genesis: Launched in July, an audited onchain token oﬀering (OTO) framework integrated with Metaplex’s dominant asset 
standard. 
● MetaDAO’s ICOs: MetaDAO’s ICOs launched in October, starting the wave for ownership coins to fundraise capital in an onchain 
manner. 
● Jupiter Decentralized Token Formation (DTF): Launched in December, an onchain ICO framework with Jup Lock escrow and 
guaranteed Meteora liquidity. 
Ownership Tokens 
Currently, there is a question of what tokenholder rights one gets when purchasing tokens. With recent acquisitions, like Coinbase acquiring 
Vector.fun or Circle acquiring Interop Labs, many called into question whether TNSR or AXL tokenholders beneﬁt at all. Many of these questions 
are likely to be answered once the CLARITY act is signed into law, but until then, the best representation of tokenholder rights is through what 
MetaDAO is calling “Ownership Tokens.” 
When a team ICOs through MetaDAO’s platform, the proceeds are locked in treasuries whose spending is gated by futarchy proposals and 
pre-deﬁned budgets and burn rates, aligning capital deployment with market-evaluated performance. The tokens that these teams issue are legally 
backed by real-world entities and IP rights, tying token ownership to enforceable claims on oﬀchain business value and reducing incentives for 
founders to abandon tokens. 
During the ICO process, teams deﬁne a target raise amount. Investors then deposit USDC into the ICO and allocations are determined by a 
               
 


---

## Page 130

129 
pro-rata model, if that target is surpassed. Project team tokens are unlocked based on performance metrics, like when a token hits a certain market 
cap, or when decided through decision market proposals. 
 
To date, seven projects have gone through MetaDAO’s ICO, raising a total of $20 million. We expect this to increase dramatically in 2026 as more 
teams look to raise onchain and provide investors conﬁdence that the token is tied to the success of the project. 
The upcoming ICO for Ranger Finance will be an important one to watch. Previously, MetaDAO’s ICO platform was not compatible with teams 
that have raised from VCs in the past or having users with project points receive a guaranteed ICO allocation. The MetaDAO team is working now 
to tweak their ICO process to include these allocations, which will grow the amount of teams that can raise through their platform. 
MetaDAO is competing with Jupiter DTF and Metaplex Genesis, and also with centralized ICO platforms like Coinbase’s Echo, Legion, and 
Coinlist. We believe that MetaDAO is in the best position going forward due to its commitment on focusing on investor protections and 
               
 


---

## Page 131

130 
tokenholder rights. In 2026 we expect to see many teams raise through their platform, which could spur natural demand for these tokens due to 
increased tokenholder guarantees. 
To stay up to date with Solana, refer to Messari’s quarterly reports written by Matthew Nay (@NaytheForceBwU). 
Enterprise Chains 
Authors: Matt Kreiser, Youssef Haidar, Alice Hou, and Austin Weiler 
XRPL 
What Went Right in 2025 
Market Performance 
 
XRP has maintained more than 4x gains it realized in Q4 2024, as its price has increased 6% year-to-date to $2.2, outperforming BTC (-3% YTD) 
               
 


---

## Page 132

131 
and ETH (-10% YTD). Moreover, XRP’s circulating market cap is up 11% YTD from $119.44 billion to $132.90 billion, as the asset maintained 
its position as the 4th largest cryptocurrency by market cap after BTC, ETH, and USDT. 
Following the election of Donald Trump in November 2024, major catalysts in 2025 included the dismissal of appeals of the SEC’s lawsuit against 
Ripple in August and the listing of spot XRP ETFs on U.S. equity markets in November. The dismissal of appeals made SDNY U.S. District 
Judge Analisa Torres' July 2023 ruling that Ripple’s programmatic sales of XRP to retail exchanges did not violate federal securities laws, but that 
its institutional sales did, the unappealed ﬁnal judgment for the case. XRP spot ETFs have seen nearly $1 billion in net ﬂows, providing another 
avenue of buy pressure alongside XRP’s strong retail ﬂows and institutional partners. 
Stablecoins and RWAs 
Stablecoins and RWA adoption on the XRPL increased signiﬁcantly in 2025. 
 
The market cap of Ripple USD (RLUSD) on the XRPL increased 11x year-to-date from $19.6 million to $235.0 million. Historically, stablecoins 
on XRPL have not had the level of adoption of major stablecoins on other networks. For example, Ethereum, TRON, Solana, and BNB Smart 
               
 


---

## Page 133

132 
Chain have stablecoin market caps of $172.0 billion, $80.4 billion, $15.2 billion, and $14.1 billion, respectively. For added context, USDT and 
USDC have market caps of $186.3 billion and $78.0 billion across all networks on which they are supported. 
However, in anticipation of increasing regulatory clarity due to the passage of the GENIUS Act in the U.S. on July 18, many stablecoin issuers 
have announced plans to launch, or have launched, stablecoins on the XRPL. Stablecoins launched in 2025 included StraitsX Digital Singapore 
dollar XSGD, euro stablecoin EURØP, Circle’s USDC, Braza Group’s USDB, and Brazilian real stablecoin BBRL. SG-Forge also plans to launch 
a euro stablecoin EURCV. To date, the market cap of these tokens is small, with USDC the second largest after RLUSD at $8.8 million. However, 
collectively they present an increased mix of stablecoin options for XRPL users. 
 
The RWA market cap on the XRPL is up 40x YTD from $5.1 million to $207.9 million as RWA oﬀerings have expanded beyond the tokenized 
short-term U.S. treasuries product TBILL to tokenized stock of market infrastructure service provider Montis Group Limited (MGL), Ondo’s 
short-term tokenized U.S. Treasury fund (OUSG), Guggenheim’s ﬁxed-income asset secured by US Treasuries (DCP), and abrdn’s short-term 
               
 


---

## Page 134

133 
tokenized treasury fund (AAULF). This ﬁrst phase of expansion has been largely driven by partnerships with Ripple. Adoption beyond these 
business development deals will hinge on institutions preferring the XRPL’s design choices and features over those of competitor chains. 
2026 Outlook 
Ripple is positioning the XRPL for institutional DeFi adoption as necessary identity, ﬁnancial, compliance, and privacy features are being 
implemented at the network level. These include multipurpose tokens (MPTs) for metadata to store RWA parameters, conﬁdential MPTs using 
Zero Knowledge Proofs (ZKPs), and credentials to control access via KYC/AML. These continued updates to make DeFi regulatorily compliant 
at the network’s base level make the XRPL increasingly attractive for institutions, providing default composability for all regulatorily compliant 
assets, as opposed to permissioned protocols on competitor chains that are by default siloed from one another. 
There are a number of developments on this front upcoming in 2026, including: 
● Conﬁdential MPTs that support privacy-preserving collateral management for token amounts (not the accounts themselves), a requirement 
for institutional adoption use cases like onchain collateral repurchase agreements and ﬁxed-income assets like Treasury bonds. 
● Permissioned Domains: Will allow institutions to require speciﬁc credentials to access their oﬀerings on the XRPL. 
● Permissioned DEX: Only accounts with valid credentials will be able to create or ﬁll orders on a permissioned domain, using the XRPL’s 
native DEX to trade assets. 
● Native Lending Protocol: A native lending and borrowing protocol is under development, utilizing single-asset vaults for crypto assets such 
as XRP, BTC, and ETH. These vaults will use credentials and permissioned domains for access control and support a number of 
compliance features, including account freezing, asset freezing, and clawback. The protocol is intended to oﬀer onchain ﬁxed-term and rate 
loans via oﬀchain underwriting, risk management, third-party custody of collateral, and an insurance fund — a model akin to that 
implemented by Maple Finance. 
Collectively, these features will deﬁne XRPL’s 2026. Organic adoption via mass issuance of regulated assets would validate the XRPL’s value 
proposition of native compliance and DeFi composability. Anything less will leave the chain where it is today, reliant on Foundation and Lab 
entities (in this case, Ripple), competing with other chains’ counterparts in business development deals for niche, regulatorily compliant stablecoin 
and RWA asset issuance, that is only a shell of the composability and capital eﬃciency DeFi at scale can deliver. 
To stay up to date with XRP Ledger, refer to Messari’s quarterly reports written by Matt Kreiser (@kreisermatt). 
Cardano 
What Went Right in 2025 
This year marked the successful activation of the Voltaire era's ﬁnal features, which fundamentally reorganized the network's upgrade and 
maintenance architecture. Cardano reached a critical turning point in September 2025 with the ﬁrst fully community-led elections for the 
Constitutional Committee (CC). By fulﬁlling the long-standing promise of a community-owned chain, the successful transfer of power 
               
 


---

## Page 135

134 
demonstrated that Cardano can survive and thrive independently of its founding entities. 
The September election replaced the interim committee controlled by founding entities with a fully community-elected committee, formally 
ending the era of founding entity control over protocol parameters. 
 
A notable highlight for the Cardano ecosystem in 2025 was the growth and diversiﬁcation of its stablecoin market cap. The aggregate stablecoin 
market cap grew by 70%, rising from $23.3 million to $39.6 million YTD. The growth in stablecoin supply provides a critical foundation needed 
to support the complex, high-volume real-world applications expected to drive the next phase of growth in 2026. The market matured from being 
heavily reliant on IUSD (whose supply contracted by 58%) to a healthier, more diverse mix of ﬁat-backed assets (USDM, USDA, USDC) and 
overcollateralized algorithmic options (DJED). 
2026 Outlook 
A key technical catalyst for 2026 is Ouroboros Leios, a major upgrade to the consensus protocol. Cardano’s throughput is bottlenecked by the 
design of its current consensus protocol, Ouroboros Praos. This leaves signiﬁcant hardware capacity unused, limiting transaction speeds. 
               
 


---

## Page 136

135 
Leios removes this limitation, allowing the network to process 1,000TPS. Instead of forcing every transaction into a single, slow line, Leios splits 
them into Input Blocks and Endorser Blocks, which allows the network to process blocks concurrently, increasing throughput. 
 
This captures the underutilized capacity shown in the chart above, raising throughput from 4.4 TxKB/s (shown in red) to nearly 300 TxKB/s 
(shown in green). By removing congestion bottlenecks, Leios enables complex, high-throughput use cases, such as institutional DeFi and 
micropayments, to run smoothly without sacriﬁcing the network's security or decentralization. 
Pentad 
Unveiled by Charles Hoskinson in December 2025, Pentad is a strategic alliance that uniﬁes the ecosystem’s ﬁve previously siloed core 
organizations, the Cardano Foundation, Emurgo, IOG, Midnight Foundation, and Intersect, into a single executive layer. 
The alliance’s immediate priority is eliminating the "island eﬀect" that has historically isolated Cardano’s economy. Pentad is focused on three 
pillars: 
               
 


---

## Page 137

136 
● Integrating Critical Infrastructure: To ensure adequate liquidity and support DeFi activity, Pentad is prioritizing integrations with 
cross-chain bridges, custodians, and stablecoin issuers. This eﬀort kicks oﬀ in early 2026 with the integration of Pyth Lazer, a low-latency 
oracle designed to support institutional-grade trading speeds. 
● Onboarding Institutions: Pentad provides a single "front door" for the ecosystem, streamlining the negotiation process to match the tempo 
of corporate partners. This consolidation eliminates the friction of the previous era, where potential partners faced a fragmented web of 
entities lacking executive authority. 
● Kingmaking Applications: Moving away from the previous strategy of broad experimentation (which spread small grants across 
thousands of unproven projects), Pentad will concentrate resources on 10 to 15 breakout applications. This "venture-style" approach is 
designed to provide the funding and operational support needed to drive these apps toward proﬁtability and tier-one exchange listings. 
To stay up to date with Cardano, refer to Messari’s quarterly reports written by Youssef Haidar (@0xYoussef_). 
Stellar 
What Went Right in 2025 
               
 


---

## Page 138

137 
 
Stellar’s real-world asset (RWA) market cap has increased 114% year-to-date (YTD) from $301.1 million to $643.9 million. The majority of this 
expansion came from BENJI, Franklin Templeton’s tokenized U.S. Treasury fund, which was the ﬁrst regulated money market fund on a 
blockchain when it launched on Stellar in April 2021. But the real story in 2025 was the expansion of RWAs on Stellar beyond BENJI to realize a 
fully mature RWA oﬀering that now includes U.S. Treasuries products like Ondo’s USDY and Spiko’s USTBL, non-U.S. debt in emerging 
markets from Etherfuse, real estate from RedSwan, and equity funds, corporate bonds, alternative institutional funds, and commodities from 
issuers such as WisdomTree and Mercado Bitcoin. 
Historically, these regulatorily compliant RWAs have been reduced to little more than a marketing gimmick providing onchain public accounting 
because they are not freely transferable, and therefore not composable within DeFi. As such, they cannot even begin to oﬀer DeFi’s core value 
proposition of greater composability and capital eﬃciency compared to their TradFi equivalents. But on Stellar, this is beginning to change with 
the launch of freely transferable RWA’s from Centrifuge and Etherfuse that can be used on overcollateralized lending and borrowing protocols like 
Blend. 
With the ﬁfth most RWAs distributed by marketcap, Stellar is a serious contender among networks vying to lead RWA issuance and is an eﬃcient 
               
 


---

## Page 139

138 
platform for institutions and retail users alike to access and interact with RWAs onchain. 
2026 Outlook 
As an L1 built to service everyday ﬁnancial use cases, Stellar’s 2026 will depend on growth in the network’s stablecoin adoption, payments, DeFi 
protocols, and RWAs. 
The vast majority of stablecoin issuance is currently on Ethereum, TRON, Solana, and BNB Chain. As a challenger to these incumbents, Stellar 
must continue to validate its near-zero transaction costs (average transaction fee of $0.00055 in Q3’25) and purpose-built products, tools, and 
applications for payments. These include more than 50 wallet applications, a global network of on and oﬀ-ramps (Anchors), and the Stellar 
Disbursements Platform (SDP), a turnkey solution for sending digital payments to many individuals for purposes such as humanitarian aid, 
micropayments, global payroll, and international creator and vendor payouts. Increased use of payment applications for purposes such as 
remittances, consumer, and B2B will also be crucial, as will increased adoption of payment ﬁnancing (PayFi) for cross-border institutional-scale 
settlement, an existing area of strength for the network. 
On the DeFi front, strong momentum from 2025 should carry into 2026. Stellar’s DeFi total-value locked has increased 4x year-to-date from 
$49.7 million to $197.1 million. In May, the Stellar Development Foundation (SDF) set a goal for Stellar to have a top 10 DeFi TVL, which would 
require $1.8 billion in TVL. After smart contracts went live on Stellar in 2024 with the release of Soroban, 2025 was the year of building out 
Stellar’s basic DeFi ecosystem and adoption. 2026, then, will be a year for Stellar to grow DeFi adoption by an order of magnitude to reach the 
top 10 DeFi TVL goal, while scaling stablecoin and payments adoption to the next wave of users. Realizing the DeFi TVL growth goal will 
require onboarding new and existing blue chip DeFi protocols and tier-1 partnerships to lock in larger deposits. It may also require incentive 
campaigns, which have historically been risky, as deposits are not sustained after the incentive campaign ends. 
To stay up to date, refer to Messari’s research reports on Stellar written by Matt Kreiser (@kreisermatt). 
Hedera 
What Went Right in 2025 
Hedera’s DeFi activity strengthened in 2025, with clear gains across both trading activity and stablecoin liquidity. Average daily DEX volume 
increased 65% YoY, rising from $5.9 million to $9.8 million, with activity heavily concentrated on SaucerSwap, Hedera’s core DEX. 
Stablecoins also had a large shift. Average stablecoin market cap climbed from $11.6 million in 2024 to $93.4 million in 2025, in part due to 
Hedera’s Q2 integration of Circle’s Cross-Chain Transfer Protocol (CCTP). By enabling native USDC transfers from Ethereum to Hedera without 
third-party bridges, CCTP improved capital mobility into the ecosystem and supported the year’s stablecoin expansion. 
               
 


---

## Page 140

139 
 
In 2025, Hedera continued to lean into institutional and public-sector adoption through regulated RWA integrations. In August, KAIO launched 
tokenized institutional fund access on Hedera for accredited and institutional investors, bringing strategies such as the Laser Digital Carry Fund, 
BlackRock ICS U.S. Dollar Liquidity Fund, and Brevan Howard Master Fund onto Hedera’s onchain rails. 
In September, the Wyoming Stable Token Commission selected Hedera as the only additional blockchain candidate for Wyoming’s Frontier Stable 
Token (FRNT), a state-issued stable token backed by dollars and Treasuries. 
2026 Outlook 
Hedera’s 2026 growth narrative centers on transforming the network into a backbone for regulated enterprise infrastructure. This evolution is 
driven by two reinforcing verticals: RWA tokenization and veriﬁable AI. By focusing on institutional utility, Hedera is positioning itself to capture 
recurring, high-volume demand within the global digital economy. 
The ﬁrst vertical, RWA tokenization, reimagines onchain settlement for national and institutional use cases. Rather than treating tokens as mere 
digital certiﬁcates, Hedera provides a robust ecosystem for the entire asset lifecycle. National-scale projects, such as Georgia’s real estate registry 
migration, leverage the network to replace manual veriﬁcation with near-instant settlement. This shift is supported by Asset Tokenization Studio, 
               
 


---

## Page 141

140 
which automates the complex legal and technical requirements of issuing digital securities, and Stablecoin Studio, which enables the 
programmable, regulated liquidity necessary to settle these transactions at scale. 
The second vertical, veriﬁable AI, introduces a trust layer for systems that require transparent and auditable computation. Partnerships with Intel, 
NVIDIA, and EQTY Lab embed cryptographic attestations at the hardware level. AI operations on NVIDIA Blackwell GPUs and Intel processors 
generate hardware-signed proofs that are recorded on the Hedera Consensus Service (HCS), creating an immutable audit trail. For example, a 
bank running an AI model to assess loan risk can produce a veriﬁable record of the model version, inputs, and outputs, allowing auditors to 
conﬁrm that decisions were generated by approved systems and not altered after the fact. 
As these eﬀorts transition into live, working deployments in 2026, Hedera’s growth narrative shifts from ecosystem experimentation to 
infrastructure adoption within regulated enterprises. This creates a clearer path to sustained network demand, driven by real settlement volume 
from RWAs and veriﬁable records for high-stakes AI systems. 
Algorand 
2025 Recap 
Staked ALGO Increase 
               
 


---

## Page 142

141 
 
A standout success for Algorand in 2025 was its increase in community staking participation following its v4.0 upgrade on Jan. 23, which enabled 
ALGO rewards for proposing blocks and wallets to delegate stake to third-party node operators. Year-to-date, total staked ALGO increased 5% 
from 1.26 billion to 1.95 billion, while community-staked ALGO rose 239% from 460.7 million to 1.56 billion. Algorand’s 2025 staking growth 
shows that reducing staking barriers and oﬀering clear incentives can boost user participation, a design worth replicating for chains struggling with 
staking participation. 
DeFi TVL Decrease 
               
 


---

## Page 143

142 
 
A key challenge for Algorand in 2025 was its sharp decline in DeFi TVL, which fell 65% from $137.6 million to $48.6 million. Throughout 2025, 
DeFi TVL remained heavily concentrated on two protocols: Folks Finance, a lending protocol with a 74% share ($35.8 million), and Tinyman, an 
AMM DEX with an 18% share ($8.8 million). 
TVL bottomed at $31.6 million on June 17 before rebounding 55% by November 30, oﬀering a modest sign of stability. However, no new 
protocols meaningfully contributed to TVL in 2025, and without diversiﬁcation, Algorand’s DeFi ecosystem, fee generation, and usage will 
remain tied to the performance of two protocols, limiting its ability to scale sustainably. 
2026 Outlook 
Algorand enters 2026 needing to expand DeFi TVL beyond Folks Finance and Tinyman. To do so, it must oﬀer stronger incentives for developers 
to launch new protocols that bring fresh capital onchain. The Foundation made early moves in this direction in 2025 by hosting ﬁve in-person 
developer events and launching the Algorand Startup Challenges, a six-week incubator with a $125,000 USDC prize pool, the largest of any 
Foundation-run hackathon to date. These initiatives marked a shift toward more competitive incentivization, but converting developer momentum 
into TVL growth remains the key challenge. Algorand’s success in 2026 will depend on its ability to attract capital across a broader set of 
               
 


---

## Page 144

143 
protocols and translate ecosystem development into DeFi TVL growth. 
To stay up to date with Algorand, refer to Messari’s quarterly reports written by Austin Weiler (@0xWeiler). 
Monolithic Chains 
Authors: Alexander Beaudry, Jeremy Koch, AJC, Jake Koch-Gallup, Matt Kreiser, Patryk Krasnicki, Matthew Nay, and Youssef Haidar 
BNB Chain 
BNB Chain cemented its position as the third-most-used blockchain in 2025, trailing only Ethereum and Solana in real adoption metrics. The 
network crossed 58 million monthly active addresses in September, overtaking Solana's 38.3 million, while daily active users consistently 
exceeded two million throughout the year. This wasn't driven by a single narrative but by broad-based ecosystem growth across DeFi, memecoins, 
and payments, all of which found a home on BNB Chain this year. 
 
               
 


---

## Page 145

144 
BNB Chain accounted for over 40% of global DEX trading volume, with $178 billion in monthly volume as of May. On May 26, trading volume 
on BNB Chain DEXs reached $13.31 billion, which was 7.9 times higher than Ethereum's $1.675 billion and 5.7 times greater than Solana's $2.32 
billion. PancakeSwap processed $420.45 billion in trading volume during the ﬁrst half of 2025 alone, while perpetuals activity surged to record 
levels when Aster launched its token on September 17, oﬀering 1,001x leverage and yield-bearing collateral through Lista DAO's liquid staking 
products. 
The memecoin narrative also returned in October after CZ's "BNB meme szn" post. Four.meme, a major launchpad on BNB Chain, brieﬂy 
surpassed Solana's Pump.fun in daily revenue, hitting $4.2 million in 24-hour fees on October 8. While Four.meme's revenue declined 89% from 
October to November as memecoin activity normalized, the platform's earlier success demonstrated that BNB Chain could capture speculative 
retail ﬂows at scale when momentum shifted in its direction. 
What made all of this possible were two critical network upgrades that transformed BNB Chain's execution environment. The Lorentz Hardfork 
on April 29 and Maxwell Hardfork on June 30 reduced block times from 3 seconds to 0.75 seconds, making BNB one of the fastest EVM chains 
in production. Transaction fees decreased by 98% to 0.05 Gwei, or approximately $0.005 per transaction. These improvements created the 
infrastructure for sustained high-frequency activity without degrading user experience, enabling BNB Chain to reliably support billions of dollars 
in daily DEX volume and millions of daily users. 
The year's biggest strategic advantage, however, was Binance's active role in directing traﬃc to BNB Chain. Binance Alpha, launched in 
December 2024, became a pre-listing showcase for early-stage tokens, and 71% of the ﬁrst wave of admitted tokens chose BNB Chain as their 
home network. The Alpha program created a gamiﬁed incentive structure where users earned points by holding assets on Binance and trading 
Alpha-listed tokens, with double points awarded for trades executed on BNB Chain via Binance Wallet. This structure funneled liquidity directly 
into BNB Chain's DEXs. BNB Chain recorded over one million new addresses daily linked to Alpha-related activity, while weekly transactions 
increased 60% and weekly trading volume climbed 115% during the initial Alpha rollout period. 
               
 


---

## Page 146

145 
 
BNB reached its all-time high at $1,373 on October 13 with a market cap of $180 billion, which put it at #3 among all crypto assets, excluding 
stablecoins, where it remained for the rest of the year. DeFi TVL increased roughly 32% year-to-date to reach $7.9 billion by November 30, while 
stablecoin supply on BNB Chain doubled to $14 billion, growing 102.9% from $6.9 billion at the beginning of the year. 
2026 Outlook 
BNB Chain enters 2026 with one major advantage: direct distribution through Binance's 290 million user base. The Binance Alpha program will 
remain central to BNB Chain's growth strategy, serving as a pipeline that funnels early-stage tokens, liquidity, and new users onto the network 
before those projects reach broader visibility. With trading competitions, point multipliers for BNB Chain transactions, and preferential treatment 
for tokens that launch on BSC, Binance has eﬀectively turned its exchange into a continuous onboarding mechanism for BNB Chain. This 
structural advantage is diﬃcult for competing chains to replicate and positions BNB Chain to capture a disproportionate share of new token 
launches and speculative retail activity in 2026. 
On the infrastructure side, the BNB Chain’s Fermi upgrade, scheduled to reach mainnet in 2026, will reduce block times to 0.45 seconds on BSC, 
targeting 40% faster transaction processing while introducing EVM optimizations and incremental state snapshots. If executed smoothly, BNB 
               
 


---

## Page 147

146 
Chain should be capable of 20,000 TPS by mid-2026 with sub-150 millisecond conﬁrmations. These improvements will expand BNB Chain's 
capacity to handle sustained high-frequency activity, particularly as perpetuals trading continues to scale and as more consumer-facing 
applications migrate to the network. 
DeFi growth in 2026 will likely concentrate around Lista DAO's lisBNB product and its integrations with Aster, PancakeSwap's lending protocols, 
and Venus Core Pool. Lista's TVL surpassed $2.85 billion in 2025, making it the third-largest protocol on BNB Chain. Lista Lending was 
launched on April 7 with $189 million in deposits within four days. The protocol became the ﬁrst to integrate World Liberty Financial's USD1 
stablecoin on BNB Chain and added mXRP, Midas's liquid-staking token for XRP, in November. If TVL continues to grow and lisBNB becomes 
standard collateral for margin trading and lending, it creates demand for BNB independent of price speculation and deepens the liquidity available 
for leveraged strategies on platforms like Aster. 
BNB Chain is also pushing into Real-World Assets. The network launched a dedicated RWA incentive program on May 29 and signed 
partnerships spanning tokenized treasuries, private credit, and real estate. Projects like Avalon Finance, OpenEden, and Matrixdock have already 
deployed yield-bearing instruments backed by oﬀchain collateral, and BNB will likely continue to push similar initiatives. 
If the Fermi upgrade lands cleanly, RWA projects continue to scale, and Binance Alpha maintains its momentum as a distribution engine, BNB 
Chain will solidify its role as the default execution layer for retail-focused DeFi, high-frequency trading, and new token launches. The network's 
combination of low fees, fast execution, and privileged access to Binance's user base creates a structural advantage that competing chains cannot 
easily counter, positioning BNB Chain for sustained growth through 2026 and beyond. 
TRON 
What Went Right in 2025 
This past year, TRON reached all-time highs in multiple areas. There have been more than 3.2 billion transactions (1.9 billion of which were free 
transactions), 2.5 million average daily active addresses, $79.36 billion in stablecoin supply, and onchain activity that generated $548.2 million in 
chain fees, the third most of any chain in 2025. 
               
 


---

## Page 148

147 
 
Chain fees have declined noticeably since September, but for good reason. On August 29, Proposal 104 was passed, lowering transaction fees by 
reducing the energy unit price by more than half, from 0.00021 TRX to 0.0001 TRX. With the stablecoin supercycle looming, TRON is 
prioritizing future growth over maximizing monetization of current platform usage, ensuring that cost-sensitive USDT users are not priced oﬀ the 
network. 
               
 


---

## Page 149

148 
 
Speaking of USDT, TRON has ﬁrmly established itself as one of the leading stablecoin settlement layers, anchored by its outsized share of USDT 
supply. TRON maintains a consistently large USDT base of $78.15 billion, representing 42% of total USDT in circulation. USDT on TRON also 
exhibits high turnover, with daily transfer volumes frequently exceeding $20-30 billion. 
This combination of scale, velocity, and consistency helps explain why TRON remains a preferred venue for global remittances, market-making 
ﬂows, and stablecoin-driven commerce. With stablecoin activity serving as a strong proxy for real economic usage, TRON’s performance 
positions it not just as a major blockchain, but as one of the core ﬁnancial rails underpinning the digital dollar ecosystem. 
2026 Outlook 
TRON is deﬁnitively one of the strongest businesses in crypto, and one of the few that can claim annualized revenues north of half a billion 
dollars. That success has not gone unnoticed. Over the past year, stablechains, purpose-built blockchains optimized speciﬁcally for stablecoin 
usage, have emerged as one of the most crowded and highly anticipated narratives in the market. These chains are explicitly designed to compete 
with TRON’s core use case: serving as the primary settlement layer for USDT. 
While expectations for some of these stablechain competitors are high, TRON’s moat should not be understated. Lower transaction fees, which 
               
 


---

## Page 150

149 
will likely be the primary advantage stablechains oﬀer, are rarely suﬃcient on their own to meaningfully change user behavior. For the marginal 
stablecoin user, what matters more is global distribution, reliable on- and oﬀ-ramps, and deep integration across exchanges, payment processors, 
merchants, and informal ﬁnancial networks. TRON’s years-long head start in distribution and integration creates a moat that newer stablechains 
will struggle to close. As a result, stablechains are perhaps better positioned to attract net-new stablecoin users and use cases rather than attempt to 
displace TRON. 
Ultimately, TRON’s challenge is not to reinvent itself, but to continue building on this distribution advantage while expanding its global footprint. 
Delivering technical upgrades that (i) optimize fees, (ii) enhance scalability and resilience, and (iii) enable fast ﬁnality and parallel execution, 
alongside continued improvements to its EVM compatibility, will be essential to retaining developers and users. If TRON can maintain its USDT 
moat while incrementally expanding its capabilities, it is well-positioned to remain a cornerstone of the global stablecoin economy in 2026. 
Sui 
What Went Right in 2025 
One of Sui’s most notable achievements in 2025 was the acceleration of onchain trading activity across AMMs, CLMMs, perpetuals, and 
orderbook venues. Rising average daily DEX volume became the clearest signal that Sui’s execution model was translating into sustained 
economic throughput. The network entered the year at $268.3 million in average daily DEX volume and expanded steadily: $305.2 million in Q1, 
$367.9 million in Q2, and $456.0 million in Q3. Momentum continued into year-end, with average daily volume reaching $557.3 million across 
October and November, supported by deeper liquidity, broader user participation, and the simultaneous growth of multiple trading venues. 
               
 


---

## Page 151

150 
 
Activity during this period was distributed across the ecosystem rather than concentrated in a single protocol. Momentum recorded $255.4 million 
in average daily volume, followed by Cetus at $87.1 million, Blueﬁn at $80.5 million, Magma at $49 million, and DeepBook at $42.2 million, 
with an additional $45 million generated by other protocols. The distribution reﬂected a structurally diversiﬁed trading ecosystem, with volume 
split across spot AMMs, CLMMs, perpetuals, and orderbook-based liquidity rather than converging on a single dominant design. 
DeFi liquidity trends reinforced this expansion. Sui’s TVL reached a high of $2.64 billion in October 2025, signaling broader capital formation 
across lending, derivatives, and BTC-backed collateral, even as levels retraced later in the quarter. 
Protocol-level execution and product improvements helped sustain the increase in trading volume. Momentum surpassed 1.3 million users and $7 
billion in cumulative volume within months of launch. Blueﬁn introduced Blueﬁn Pro, adding a new margining engine and native USDC support. 
DeepBook expanded into margin trading and nearly tripled cumulative volume. 
Sui’s underlying infrastructure enabled low-cost, high-throughput trading across venues. Average transaction costs stayed below one cent, 32% of 
all transactions were sponsored, and core developer tools improved meaningfully through new passkey authentication, MPC wallet integrations, 
               
 


---

## Page 152

151 
and the expansion of Walrus, Seal, Nautilus, and Ika. 
By the end of 2025, Sui demonstrated that its performance advantages could sustain real economic activity at scale. Liquidity broadened, DEX 
volumes climbed, and the network consistently delivered predictable, low-latency execution across a diverse mix of trading venues. The next 
phase of growth will depend on how eﬀectively Sui uniﬁes its expanding infrastructure stack into a cohesive platform. 
2026 Outlook 
 
Sui enters 2026 with the opportunity to evolve from a high-performance execution environment into a cohesive full-stack platform. Over the past 
two years, the network has assembled a broad set of capabilities spanning onboarding, identity, storage, compute, liquidity, and cross-chain 
coordination. The strategic question for 2026 is whether these components can operate as a uniﬁed surface that lowers development friction and 
enables applications to compose functionality natively rather than integrate disparate protocols. If 2025 showed that Sui can support real economic 
               
 


---

## Page 153

152 
activity at scale, 2026 will test whether the Sui Stack can turn those capabilities into a coherent platform for builders. 
A number of Sui’s primitives already push in this direction. Sponsored transactions, zkLogin, and Passkey support give developers tools to 
minimize onboarding friction and oﬀer authentication patterns familiar to mainstream users. On the liquidity side, DeepBook provides a uniﬁed 
orderbook layer supporting AMMs, CLMMs, aggregators, and derivatives platforms, while the Sui Bridge and Ika introduce native cross-chain 
movement and MPC-based coordination. 
Storage, compute, and privacy primitives deepen this foundation. Walrus oﬀers decentralized blob storage for large assets, Nautilus enables 
veriﬁable oﬀchain computation through trusted execution environments, and Seal provides encrypted access control for sensitive data. 
Higher-level components such as Sui Kiosk and the Sui Stack Messaging SDK simplify commerce ﬂows, asset management, and application-level 
communication. 
In the base case, 2026 will be deﬁned by increasing cohesion across these layers. Developer activity should grow as integration friction declines 
and stack primitives mature into a more coherent platform. Liquidity is becoming more uniﬁed through DeepBook integrations and improved 
routing, supporting both spot and derivatives markets. Apps in AI, commerce, gaming, and data services will deploy production versions that use 
Walrus, Seal, and Nautilus for storage, privacy, and compute. Taken together, these trends support steady ecosystem growth, broader usage of Sui’s 
primitives, and a more diverse distribution of onchain activity.

Aptos 
What Went Right in 2025 
               
 


---

## Page 154

153 
 
Aptos’s stablecoin market cap has increased 114% year-to-date (YTD) from $627.8 million to $1.51 billion. Native USDC, USDT, and BUIDL 
contracts were launched on the network in October and November 2024, paving the way for market cap growth in 2025. World Liberty Financial’s 
USD1 also launched in October 2025. Together, these stablecoins enabled Aptos’s record stablecoin transfer volume, which grew 5.6x from $8.6 
billion in the month of January to $48.4 billion in November. Additionally, LayerZero’s omnichain interoperability framework made Paxos’s 
Global Dollar Stablecoin (USDG) available in November and PayPal’s PYUSD in September, while bridged token contracts for Ethena’s USDe 
and sUSDE were launched on Aptos in February. As Aptos moves towards technically realizing its vision of becoming “the global trading 
engine,” stablecoin usage is a leading area of growth and adoption. 
2026 Outlook 
In a future where all assets are tokenized and tradable onchain, capital markets operate 24/7 without intermediaries, and access is permissionless, 
Aptos’s goal is to become the global trading engine. Technical capacity and adoption are the two variables Aptos Labs and the Aptos Foundation 
need to solve for to reach this goal. 
               
 


---

## Page 155

154 
Technical Capacity 
Aptos is already one of the most performant L1 blockchains, but will look to scale even further in 2026. Median block times are now 60ms as 
more than 97% of validators have adopted the Velociraptr upgrade, which reduced block times by 40%. Building on Velociraptr, block times will 
scale even further to 10ms via Archon’s architecture. In the context of ﬁnancial markets, this will allow market makers to quote tighter, manage 
orders more eﬃciently leading to better pricing, trade nearly instantaneously, and reduce time between order book matches. 
Further upgrades to reduce latency and boost throughput on Aptos include the Block-STM V2 upgrade, improving upon Block-STM dynamic 
parallel execution to enable thousands of complex transactions to run simultaneously. Zaptos will optimize Aptos’ execution further via optimistic 
execution and commitment, while Shardines will introduce a horizontally scaled execution engine to process partitions of transactions in parallel 
across multiple nodes. In testing, this approach has already enabled Aptos to achieve one million TPS with 30 shards. Finally, encrypted 
mempools will keep transaction details hidden until block inclusion, preventing frontrunning, and ensuring conﬁdentiality for traders. 
Adoption 
Decibel and Shelby are the two main products being developed to drive adoption on Aptos under its global trading vision. 
Now in testnet, Decibel is a fully onchain permissionless trading engine that uniﬁes spot, perps, and margin into a single programmable, global 
platform. Anticipated to go live Q1 2026, Decibel delivers the performance of centralized exchanges with the transparency, control, and 
composability of DeFi. 
Co-developed by Aptos Labs and Jump Crypto, Shelby is a cloud-grade hot storage protocol for data availability. Currently in Devnet, Shelby is 
designed to deliver Web2-grade low-latency with sub-second reads and high-throughput storage suitable for real-time, read-intensive Web3 
applications for content streaming, AI inference and real-time applications. Shelby’s coordination and settlement is on Aptos, though the 
underlying storage functionality is chain-agnostic. The protocol runs via nodes connected by a ﬁber-optic network that will be rewarded in 
real-time for providing data. 
To stay up to date, refer to Messari’s research reports on Aptos written by Matt Kreiser (@kreisermatt). 
Sei 
What Went Right in 2025 
Sei had an incredible year with consistent growth across key metrics, the ﬁrst ecosystem token launches, and partnerships with core infrastructure 
providers. Network activity has grown for ﬁve straight quarters, largely led by what is now a leading gaming ecosystem in crypto. Average daily 
active addresses (DAAs) and average daily transactions are at all-time highs, led by games like World of Dypians, Sugar Senpai, and Idle Glory. 
               
 


---

## Page 156

155 
 
Growth wasn’t limited to gaming. Sei’s DeFi ecosystem had an equally strong year with TVL, spot trading volume, and stablecoin market cap 
continually reaching new all-time highs throughout 2025 while ecosystem tokens of leading DeFi protocols like DragonSwap (DRG) and Yei 
Finance (CLO) launched in July and October. Spot trading volume in particular was a standout, with cumulative spot trading volume reaching 
$9.47 billion. Sei is on track to surpass $10 billion in spot trading volume in 2025, which should mark more than 400% YoY growth relative to the 
$2.66 billion facilitated in 2024. 
As for token price, SEI’s performance hasn’t matched the performance of the network’s fundamentals, as price has dropped 69% YTD from $0.42 
to $0.13. That said, the token’s circulating market cap rank stayed relatively ﬂat going from 65th to 69th, indicating the token performed in line 
with the broader market. 
Looking ahead, onchain central limit order books (CLOBs) are emerging on Sei, bringing more optimal architecture for capital eﬃciency, price 
discovery, and scalability. Citrex Markets and Oxium have launched, but the most signiﬁcant is still to come. Monaco Protocol is a perpetual 
futures exchange being incubated by Sei Labs. With Sei’s Giga upgrade looming, the network is primed to return to its roots by creating a 
next-gen CLOB to compete with Hyperliquid. 
2026 Outlook 
               
 


---

## Page 157

156 
Despite a momentous 2025, Sei’s DeFi ecosystem was negatively impacted by the defaults of Stream Finance and Elixir in early November, 
which caused similar eﬀects across other ecosystems. The network’s TVL and stablecoin market cap halved in the days that followed, ending a 
great year on a sour note. Sei will need to rebound via asset inﬂows and continued excitement to use its DeFi protocols in 2026. Sei can lean on 
the host of partnerships it secured this year for increased distribution, including native USDC, integrations with Backpack Wallet and Metamask, 
and upcoming launches of PYUSD, AUSD, and USDY. 
On the technical side, Sei Labs will be key to 2026. Development of Sei’s next major upgrade, Giga, is well underway. The upgrade hopes to oﬀer 
a 50x improvement in throughput over other EVM-compatible networks by reaching a maximum capacity of ﬁve gigagas per second. This level of 
performance would be achieved by revamped execution, consensus (Autobahn), and storage, as well as the ﬁrst-ever instance of multiple 
concurrent proposers on an EVM L1, allowing multiple validators to propose transactions simultaneously. 
Giga will enable new use cases, such as that of Monaco Protocol. With leadership from Jayendra Jog, Co-founder of Sei and former Software 
Engineer at Robinhood, and Simranjeet Singh, CEO and Co-founder of Monaco Protocol and former Head of DeFi Trading at GSR, Sei has a 
clear catalyst for increased DeFi activity in 2026 via Monaco Protocol. 
To stay up to date with Sei, refer to Messari’s quarterly reports written by Patryk Krasnicki (@Solofunk). 
Flow 
What Went Right in 2025 
Widely regarded as the most signiﬁcant technical milestone in the network’s history, Forte advanced Flow beyond its reputation as a consumer 
blockchain into high-performance, general-purpose infrastructure capable of supporting complex institutional ﬁnance and automated agentic 
workﬂows. 
The upgrade introduced scheduled transactions, a protocol-native “cron job” enabling automated DeFi strategies without oﬀchain dependencies. 
Simultaneously, native WebAuthn and Passkey support replaced the need for seed phrases with biometric authentication, enabling native mobile 
onboarding through device-backed credentials. 
               
 


---

## Page 158

157 
 
A standout success for Flow in 2025 was the explosive expansion of its DeFi ecosystem, where TVL surged 185% from $37.5 million to $106.9 
million. 
This was driven by a structural maturity in DeFi markets, which evolved beyond swaps to support more complex and creative DeFi primitives, 
such as MORE Markets’ omnichain vaults and KittyPunch’s decentralized volatility index protocol, enabling users to earn yield from the price 
changes of Flow EVM assets. Both protocols incentivized TVL by oﬀering high APRs on bridged PYUSD (USDF) pools. 
By successfully bootstrapping a layer of complex, yield-bearing infrastructure, Flow has established the necessary ﬁnancial infrastructure to 
support the strategic push towards Consumer DeFi. 
2026 Outlook 
DeFi has had a highly technical barrier to entry and is historically fraught with risk, ranging from exploits to liquidations. This has hindered 
adoption among non-crypto natives. In 2026, Flow is focused on bridging the gap between consumer ﬁnance and DeFi with the launch of Flow 
Credit Markets (FCM), a lending protocol enabling mainstream users to leverage high DeFi yields while mitigating liquidations and smart contract 
risk. 
               
 


---

## Page 159

158 
Dapper Labs is commercializing Flow’s infrastructure with Peak Money, a mobile wallet built on top of the FCM. By abstracting away seed 
phrases and technical hurdles, the app repackages DeFi transactions into a simple, “deﬁbank” interface, addressing the usability concerns that 
have long restricted crypto to niche audiences. 
 
Beyond the app itself, Peak Money establishes a new operational standard for the Flow ecosystem: 
1. The Foundation builds the permanent, enshrined utility. 
2. Strategic Partners launch applications to commercialize the utility. 
3. The Community inherits a robust, liquid foundation with a sustainable revenue model. 
By hardening ﬁnancial primitives such as FCM directly into the protocol, rather than relying on third-party contracts, Flow is vertically integrating
