information aggregation, more stable liquidity, and improved calibration, reducing structural biases without altering market fundamentals. Several 
protocols have already begun implementing these ideas, integrating AI-driven forecasting, agent participation, and decisn-support tooling into 
existing market designs. 
In this sense, AI is not an optional enhancement, but a necessary participation layer for prediction markets to mature into durable forecasting 
infrastructure. 
DePIN is the Frontier 
Author: Dylan Bane 
               
 


---

## Page 251

250 
Key Themes 
● DePIN networks that vertically integrate, incorporating resources into ﬁnished enterprise/consumer facing products are best positioned to 
generate sustainable revenue and capture higher margins, helping solve the demand side. 
● DePAI data collection protocols are positioned to break out in 2026 as demand for scarce real-world data accelerates, enabled by 
DePIN-style incentives that support faster and more scalable collection than centralized solutions. 
● InfraFi will emerge as a breakout DePIN-adjacent category by connecting onchain capital to net-new, infrastructure niches underserved by 
traditional private credit such as debt ﬁnancing. 
● Regulatory clarity will expand the DePIN builder base and accelerate corporate entry by reducing uncertainty around token design and 
making enterprise-integrated DePIN models more feasible. 
● DePIN could exceed $100 million in onchain veriﬁed revenue in 2026, as established protocols scale from seven to eight ﬁgure annual 
revenues and new blue chip DePINs TGE. 
Introduction 
2025 was deﬁned by steady growth in fundamentals and a few big wins for the DePIN sector 
The year’s developments can be grouped into four core themes: 
● Strong growth in veriﬁed revenue, signaling early product–market ﬁt among leading networks (~$55 million in total annualized revenue). 
● Greater emphasis on transparency, with revenue and usage increasingly veriﬁable onchain. 
● A shift away from total addressable market narratives toward fundamentals, positioning DePIN as one of crypto’s most substantive 
application layers. 
● Continued experimentation across token design, go-to-market strategy, and infrastructure ﬁnancing, laying the groundwork for more 
scalable and sustainable protocols. 
This year marked a sharp contrast with 2024, which was deﬁned by rapid token price appreciation, narrative momentum, and heavy fundraising 
across nearly every DePIN subsector. Excitement was driven by early success stories, most notably Helium Mobile’s growth from zero to over 
100,000 users, as well as DePIN’s overlap with dominant crypto narratives around AI, GPU compute, and data generation. 
That enthusiasm pulled a young sector, one building real-world infrastructure on Web2-like timelines, into crypto-style valuations disconnected 
from present fundamentals. When broader crypto markets weakened in early 2025 following the start of the new U.S. administration, DePIN 
token prices fell sharply and failed to recover, declining roughly 56% year-to-date. 
The decline in token prices grounded DePIN closer to its real progress. Revenue growth continued in 2025 at a pace consistent with companies 
that are, in most cases, less than three years old. 
Nevertheless, DePIN occupied an uncomfortable middle ground for public investors. Narrative-driven traders discounted revenue-backed tokens, 
               
 


---

## Page 252

251 
while fundamental investors viewed price-to-sales multiples as still overly inﬂated. No investor segment could fully get behind DePIN or 
champion it. 
Even so, by late 2025 the broader crypto backdrop began to turn more favorable. New L1 and L2 launches underperformed expectations, 
memecoin activity waned, and attention shifted toward assets with real revenue, buybacks, and measurable value accrual. Tokens such as HYPE 
and PUMP, generating among the highest onchain revenues, emerged as the new models for success. Fundamentals, cash ﬂow, and P/S multiples 
moved back to the center of the crypto conversation. 
In this seeming new environment, DePIN is well positioned for the next phase of crypto’s evolution. Its deﬁning characteristics, real-world utility, 
observable demand, and growing revenue, align closely with where the market is headed. The open question is execution: whether DePIN 
networks can continue scaling revenue and mature into large, durable businesses. 
Our 2026 DePIN theses focus on the strategies and subsectors most likely to shape this next phase, from how networks scale revenue and capture 
value to which emerging verticals are positioned to break out. 
Vertical Integration Solves the DePIN Demand Side 
Most DePIN networks produce commoditized resources that struggle to tap into large-scale sustainable demand. 
The most proﬁtable models will be those that tightly integrate their DePIN-derived resources into vertically integrated, end-to-end products 
that go Direct-2-Consumer (D2C). The shift toward verticalization is already underway, with Helium Mobile leading as the number one DePIN 
by revenue ($20.1 million annualized), while upcoming players like Daylight and Fuse quietly build the largest real-world facing businesses in 
crypto, incorporating DePIN into their verticalized stack behind the scenes. 
               
 


---

## Page 253

252 
 
Commodity Resources Obtain Commodity Margins 
Early DePIN networks were built on the belief that they could scale by generating large volumes of raw resources and selling them directly into 
open markets. The assumption was that abundant community supplied hardware would allow these networks to compete primarily on price for 
resources such as GPU compute, bandwidth and storage, while also oﬀering performance advantages like lower latency through more distributed 
edge architectures. 
In practice, generated revenue was lackluster. 
A number of DePINs assumed the problem was a lack of sales and marketing support to sell the raw resources. In response, many protocols 
created gateway companies or foundations that operated as dedicated sales and marketing arms for the network. This approach was eﬀective at 
generating early traction and producing initial revenue in the six to seven ﬁgure range, but it has not translated into greater scale, and most DePINs 
have been unable to grow these eﬀorts into eight ﬁgure revenue and beyond. 
Part of the problem is that selling undiﬀerentiated commoditized resources is inherently a low margin business. Competing in this environment 
               
 


---

## Page 254

253 
requires oﬀering the lowest possible price, which forces networks to depend heavily on high sales volume to generate meaningful revenue. 
Commodity resources are: 
● Interchangeable regardless of who provides them. 
● Market competition tends to drive prices toward the cost of production. 
● Supply is abundant, which limits pricing power. 
● Scaling revenue depends heavily on volume rather than premium pricing. 
DePINs have simply not been able to generate enough volume to compensate for low margins. 
The issue is multifaceted but can be distilled into two primary obstacles: 
1. Lack of access to end consumersEnd consumers are willing to pay a premium for integrated, user-facing products, but they have little 
need for raw commoditized resources. Most DePINs never reach this customer segment, which limits their ability to capture higher margin 
revenue. 
2. Limited adoption by businesses that already build integrated productsBusinesses that could theoretically use these resources tend to 
rely on established supply chains or operate with technical and operational setups that are not compatible with resources produced through 
DePIN networks. This reduces the pool of viable enterprise buyers and reinforces the challenge of scaling demand. 
For the most part, selling low-margin raw resources is likely not a winning strategy for DePINs. 
The solution might lie in increasing margins by delivering a vertically integrated product with high margins that can tap into both consumer and 
enterprise markets. 
Vertical Integration Turns DePIN Resources Into Usable Products 
Packaging DePIN derived resources into complete consumer or enterprise facing products increases margins, lowering the relative volume 
required to scale revenues. By launching a full end-to-end product, DePINs can increase proﬁtability and revenue growth, accelerating the DePIN 
ﬂywheel and as a result token value. 
Vertical integration increases value created by DePIN networks: 
● It moves DePINs out of low margin commodity markets and into higher margin integrated products that can command premium pricing. 
● It expands the customer base by enabling direct access to end consumers and enterprises. 
● It creates meaningful diﬀerentiation, reducing the race to the bottom that deﬁnes commoditized resource markets. 
● It strengthens long term token value by tying the network to multiple higher value economic activities instead of a single commodity 
output. 
● It creates tighter feedback loops between users and the network, enabling faster product iteration and alignment with customer demand. 
The winning formula is not to create a resource and hope that demand eventually appears. The winning formula is to build the full product stack 
               
 


---

## Page 255

254 
around that resource. We expect that a large share of the most successful and proﬁtable DePIN networks will adopt verticalized product strategies 
going forward. 
Helium Mobile: A Blueprint for Verticalization 
Helium Mobile is the strongest proof point that verticalization works. Instead of selling bandwidth as a generic commodity, Helium Mobile 
delivers a full consumer wireless product by doing the following: 
● Bundling hotspot coverage into a mobile service. 
● Handling onboarding, billing, SIM provisioning, and customer support. 
● Integrating hotspot coverage, coverage maps, and network fallback into one uniﬁed experience. 
● Delivering a consumer-ready mobile oﬀering built on decentralized infrastructure. 
This approach has reshaped Helium’s economics. The network now generates $21 million in annualized revenue, and Helium Mobile accounts for 
53% of HNT and Data Credit burns. The majority of value accrual is therefore driven by a single Mobile Virtual Network Operator (MVNO) 
rather than the broader carrier oﬄoad network with partners like AT&T and T-Mobile. 
               
 


---

## Page 256

255 
 
The reason is straightforward. Helium Mobile burns 100% of its subscription revenue from its $15 and $30 monthly plans. Even though Helium 
Mobile Oﬄoad burns far less HNT than carrier oﬄoad in a given period, the MVNO generates far more revenue because it sells a higher margin, 
vertically integrated mobile service directly to consumers. In the week of Dec 8, Helium Mobile Oﬄoad burned $6,700 of HNT compared to 
$201,377 from carrier oﬄoad, yet Helium Mobile generated $216,000 that week in subscription revenue that ﬂowed entirely to HNT holders 
through burns. 
This model changes DePIN unit economics. Instead of competing to sell the cheapest bandwidth to enterprise carriers, Helium captures much 
higher margins by selling a complete wireless product to end users. The result is the ﬁrst DePIN with veriﬁable 8-ﬁgure revenue at $21 million 
annualized. It demonstrates that meaningful scale comes not from selling raw bandwidth but from turning decentralized bandwidth into a 
verticalized mobile service. 
Longer term, Helium Mobile may shift to burning a portion of bottom-line proﬁt rather than all top-line revenue for sustainability, but even then 
the verticalized model is likely to remain far more value accretive than commodity sales. 
               
 


---

## Page 257

256 
This is the diﬀerence between commodity exposure and full-stack product ownership. 
Other Vertically Integrated Approaches 
Emerging networks across multiple sectors highlight the advantages of verticalization. 
Filecoin 
  Filecoin initially launched as a decentralized network optimized for long-term, cost-eﬃcient (“cold”) storage. Over time, the protocol expanded 
beyond this narrow use case through a series of architectural and ecosystem developments, including tighter IPFS integration, improvements to 
retrieval markets, the introduction of Filecoin Plus and its allocator program to onboard higher-quality and enterprise-grade datasets, and, most 
notably, the launch of the Filecoin Virtual Machine (FVM), which added onchain programmability and application-level coordination. 
 
Together, these changes have moved Filecoin toward a vertically integrated decentralized infrastructure stack, supporting not only storage, but also 
payments, programmability, data access, and service composition. Historically, many teams were reluctant to migrate from centralized cloud 
providers like AWS due to high switching costs, limited service coverage, and poor developer and user experience. While these challenges have 
               
 


---

## Page 258

257 
not disappeared entirely, Filecoin’s expanded infrastructure, enterprise integrations, and onchain coordination primitives have materially improved 
the cost–beneﬁt equation for certain Web3, data-intensive, and veriﬁable compute workloads. 
Daylight 
Daylight is a renewable energy company that installs distributed energy resources such as solar panels and batteries. It encourages users to connect 
these assets to the Daylight network through forthcoming token rewards, allowing Daylight to access ﬂexible energy capacity and the associated 
data. 
Energy data and user-granted ﬂexibility are not commodities. A household can only make its energy available to one network or Virtual Power 
Plant (VPP) at a time. The DePIN layer is therefore embedded within a larger technical stack that standardizes energy data and makes ﬂexible 
capacity usable for downstream VPPs and energy markets. 
Daylight is vertically integrated end to end. It sources Distributed Energy Resource (DER) connections, gains access to the energy and data 
through the network, and sells a diﬀerentiated product to energy buyers. 
Fuse 
Fuse operates a broader energy stack than Daylight. It handles energy generation, retail sales, and VPP operations within a single system. Rather 
than selling capacity and data to independent VPPs, Fuse operates its own VPP and uses its ENERGY network to attract supply. 
Traditional VPP incentives often amount to only $4 to $5 per month and must be paid out in cash. Fuse uses token incentives to signiﬁcantly 
increase the amount of ﬂexible capacity it can access while lowering its cost of acquisition. These savings then fund customer discounts and 
rewards within the Fuse energy ecosystem. 
Fuse does not sell its DePIN-derived resource to third parties, yet it still demonstrates the power of vertical integration. The DePIN network 
ampliﬁes the economics of a much larger value stack. 
Conclusion 
The DePIN networks that will endure are not commodity resource sellers. They will be vertically integrated platforms that transform decentralized 
supply into complete products with clear customers, clear distribution, and clear economics. Verticalization shifts how demand is created and 
captured, which raises the next question: which resource categories naturally support full stack integration, and which ones are structurally bound 
to commoditization? 
Regulatory Clarity Opens the Door to Corporate DePINs and Lowers the Barrier to Entry for 
Entrepreneurs 
As the SEC moves toward a clear framework for DePIN token regulation, including no-action letters issued to DoubleZero and Fuse and explicit 
signaling that high-value real-world utility networks will be protected, the regulatory derisking will unlock a wave of non-crypto corporate 
               
 


---

## Page 259

258 
participation and dramatically lower barriers for new entrepreneurs entering the DePIN space. 
 
First Steps Towards a Dedicated SEC Framework for DePIN 
The most important shift underway is that the SEC is increasingly recognizing that not all tokens resemble ﬁnancial instruments. 
● They are directly tied to the consumption of real physical services such as bandwidth, compute, storage, mapping, or energy, giving them 
functional utility beyond purely ﬁnancial use. 
● Their primary economic role is to meter, allocate, and settle access to decentralized infrastructure, making real usage a core driver of value 
even when speculation exists. 
● They incentivize deployment and operation of real-world hardware, creating supply-side growth dynamics that traditional crypto tokens 
               
 


---

## Page 260

259 
and securities do not address. 
● They do not provide ownership claims, revenue rights, or contractual proﬁt expectations, distinguishing them from securities even when 
governance or speculative elements are present. 
An SEC framework that explicitly carves out DePIN tokens as non-securities is more than a regulatory nuance. It would represent the ﬁrst major 
structural shift in crypto policy since the Genius Act and brings legal certainty to an area where ambiguity has long constrained institutional 
adoption, capital formation, and entrepreneurial risk-taking. 
No-Action Relief for DoubleZero and Fuse Establishes the First Precedents 
The issuance of no-action letters for DoubleZero and Fuse creates the ﬁrst real-world precedents for compliant DePIN token models. These 
decisions matter for two reasons. 
First, they represent a test case that demonstrates the SEC’s willingness to diﬀerentiate between: tokens designed for utility and physical service 
provision versus tokens that constitute investment vehicles. 
Second, they give founders and investors the ﬁrst signs of a compliance blueprint for launching tokens tied to physical work, micro-payments, 
bandwidth, compute, and other DePIN primitives. 
That alone lowers the cost of capital, derisks token design, and improves founder willingness to build in the United States. 
Corporate Entry Accelerates Once Legal Risk Falls 
Corporate participation accelerates once legal risk falls. A clear DePIN framework opens the door for entry across several categories: 
● Telecom carriers can deploy last-mile bandwidth, oﬄoad traﬃc, and extend coverage through DePIN networks. 
● Utilities and energy companies can integrate rooftop solar, home batteries, EV chargers, and smart-grid nodes as supply into energy 
DePINs for internal or external VPPs. 
● Autonomous vehicle companies can incentivize the contribution of real-time mobility data, mapping updates, and sensor feeds that enhance 
network intelligence. 
● Robotics manufacturers can operate distributed ﬂeets that earn tokens for physical tasks and high-value embodied data collection. 
● Logistics and supply chain operators can connect IoT sensors, telematics devices, and asset trackers to open networks for routing and 
visibility. 
These companies already operate infrastructure at global scale. What they have lacked is a compliant, standardized, and economically aligned way 
to participate in open physical networks. Regulatory clarity provides exactly that. 
Corporations are also uniquely positioned to beneﬁt from verticalization. By integrating a DePIN network into their existing stack, they can 
reduce operating costs, accelerate infrastructure buildout, and improve the performance of their own products and services. 
               
 


---

## Page 261

260 
We are already seeing Inversion Capital attempt to acquire an MVNO in Mexico, integrate Helium to lower connectivity costs for subscribers, and 
use that distribution to onboard users into its Inversion L1 chain and DeFi products as the ﬁrst acquisition in a permanent capital vehicle. 
 
It is too early to validate Inversion’s experiment, but the approach may point us towards the future of corporate DePIN adoption. By acquiring 
distribution and embedding DePIN to improve eﬃciency, Inversion highlights how corporations may be already positioned to leverage their 
existing customer access while capturing the performance and cost advantages that DePIN networks provide. 
Altogether enabling corporate DePIN adoption is a step-change in the potential scale of DePIN, shifting the model from crypto-native to 
enterprise-integrated. 
Entrepreneurial Barriers Collapse as DePIN Is “Derisked” 
               
 


---

## Page 262

261 
Founders have long been discouraged by regulatory uncertainty. A clear DePIN framework removes the two biggest friction points: 
● The fear that launching a token could trigger enforcement or be deemed illegal. 
● The diﬃculty of designing compliant token economies in the absence of clear standards or precedent. 
Just as crypto has seen an inﬂux of talent into the stablecoin sector following the regulatory clarity provided by the Genius Act for stablecoins , 
similar clarity within DePIN would expand the founder pool and signiﬁcantly increase the number of new DePIN startups entering the market. 
When the gray zone disappears, the sector no longer contends with regulatory risk and instead beneﬁts from regulatory tailwinds. 
DePAI Protocols Break Out as Real-World Data Demand Surges With a Handful of Investable Tokens 
2026 
 
Demand for real-world data is accelerating as physical AI models move toward large-scale training. Because DePAI can uniquely scale the 
collection of high-quality physical data, the small number of credible DePAI networks that launch in 2026 and prove real revenue are likely to see 
outsized demand for their tokens. 
If physical AI ultimately requires data at the digital AI, the ecosystem remains two to four orders of magnitude short. Open and commercial 
               
 


---

## Page 263

262 
robotics datasets currently sit in the 10³ to 10⁵ hour range, roughly where language models were in the pre-GPT-3 era. In practical terms, physical 
AI is nearly a decade behind digital AI on raw data scale, which is exactly the gap DePAI is positioned to close. 
By turning globally distributed robots and sensors into crypto-incentivized data collectors, DePAI can scale physical data generation faster than 
any centralized actor. 
Physical AI’s Hard Bottleneck: Real-World Data 
Physical AI models require millions of hours of real-world data to be trained eﬀectively, yet today’s robotics datasets remain in the low-thousands 
of hours, and even the largest commercial collectors like Scale AI only report around 100 thousand hours of usable physical data. This is two to 
four orders of magnitude below what embodied-AI scaling curves suggest is necessary. With compute controlled by giants like NVIDIA and 
models operated by Big Tech incumbents like OpenAI and Google, the greatest opportunity in advancing physical AI development is high-quality, 
diverse, real-world data. 
This is where DePAI holds unique structural advantages. 
DePAI uses DePIN-like incentives to incentivize the deployment of distributed robots and sensors to scale physical data collection faster and more 
broadly than centralized data collection: 
● Scale: Thousands of independent robot and sensor operators deployed across geographies, not a single corporate ﬂeet. 
● Quality: Structured, high-ﬁdelity, veriﬁable data tied to speciﬁc tasks and environments, guaranteed by cryptographic proofs. 
● Diversity: Heterogeneous hardware, climates, scenes, and contexts, the long-tail variation physical AI models require for broad 
generalization. 
The DePAI Stack Is Broad, But Only Data Collection Presents an Immediate Monetization Opportunity 
The DePAI stack has a wide range of layers (Simpliﬁed): 
               
 


---

## Page 264

263 
 
Most of these layers are multiple years away from large-scale enterprise adoption or protocol-level revenue. 
However, one component is economically viable right now – Real-world data collection. 
AI companies are already paying for: 
● Navigation data 
● Video streams 
● 3D maps 
● Sensor logs 
● Telematics 
● Geospatial signals 
● Long-tail environment footage 
DePAI data collection protocols can ﬁll speciﬁc gaps in these areas, creating a short term monetization opportunity. 
               
 


---

## Page 265

264 
Data Collection DePINs are Already Generating Millions In Revenue 
Several existing DePINs already generate real revenue from data sales, showing that AI demand is real and immediate: 
● Hivemapper ($2.1 million annualized revenue): Roadside mapping data for navigation and AI training use cases. 
● DIMO ($257,000 annualized revenue): Vehicle telematics data. 
● Geodnet ($5.1 million annualized revenue): RTK and GNSS data. 
● ROVR ($232,000 annualized revenue): Drone imagery and aerial mapping. 
These networks sell directly into industries that overlap with physical AI training: mapping, navigation, geolocation, autonomous driving, 
simulation, and world-model grounding. They are already serving DePAI use cases, just not as purpose-built robotics data engines. 
The next evolution is DePAI networks designed speciﬁcally to capture robotics-grade, embodied-AI training data. 
DePAI Data Collection is the Most Immediate Opportunity 
Three upcoming projects stand out as the ﬁrst purpose-built DePAI data collectors: 
● BitRobot: BitRobot is a crypto-incentivized, decentralized platform for embodied AI research and robotics data built on Solana with a 
subnet-based architecture. It brings together robots, compute, datasets, and human collaborators into modular subnets that generate 
real-world data, models, and benchmarks to accelerate progress in embodied AI. Participants contribute hardware, data, and compute in 
return for rewards, while the network supports a marketplace of valuable resources that others can rent or use to drive AI breakthroughs. 
● PrismaX: PrismaX is a decentralized robotics data and teleoperations platform backed by $11 million in funding, focused on solving the 
data bottleneck in physical AI and robotics. The protocol aggregates high-quality, multimodal interaction and sensor data from robots and 
human-in-the-loop teleoperations to fuel machine learning models that cannot be trained through simulation or text alone. By standardizing 
remote operation and incentivizing data contributors, Prismax aims to create a scalable data ﬂywheel that bridges the gap between current 
robotics capabilities and the needs of next-generation physical AI models. 
● Poseidon is a full-stack data network focused on producing IP-cleared, high-quality long-tail datasets for AI, with explicit consent, 
licensing, and provenance baked in. It targets data bottlenecks in areas like humanoid robotics, autonomous driving edge cases, and 
multimodal pre-training by bridging distributed collection with structured curation and labeling workﬂows. 
These collectors sit directly in front of real demand. If they validate revenue, the market will have almost no alternatives to consider. 
After Data: Processing, Coordination & Spatial Layers 
The coordination layers of DePAI, which involve establishing universal identity and settlement between autonomous agents, will be critical for 
long-term scale, but are not immediate revenue drivers. These teams round out the DePAI ecosystem but will scale adoption later: 
● peaq is an L1 purpose-built for the “machine economy,” focused on helping DePIN apps bring devices, robots, and machines onchain and 
               
 


---

## Page 266

265 
monetize real-world activity. It positions itself as the coordination layer plus protocol standards that make machine networks interoperable 
and economically usable. 
● IoTeX is an L1 ecosystem focused on “real-world AI,” aiming to transform data from physical machine networks into collective 
intelligence that can power next-generation AI systems. It’s positioned as an open stack for DePIN-style machine data, identity, and 
coordination for connected devices. 
● Auki is building a “real-world web” that makes physical spaces browsable, navigable, and searchable for AI, centered around its posemesh 
and spatial infrastructure. The network is designed to provide machines and agents with a shared, decentralized understanding of space 
through visual positioning and spatial computing primitives. 
● OpenMind is building OM1, an open-source, AI-native operating system for robots, positioned as an “Android for robots” that helps 
robots perceive, reason, and act across diﬀerent hardware. It pairs OM1 with FABRIC, a decentralized coordination layer for trust and 
collaboration among robots and agents. 
All of these teams are compelling, but none are positioned to generate revenue on a 2026 timeline in the same way that DePAI data collection 
protocols are. 
The Grand Prize: Proprietary Physical AI Models and Operating Systems 
Over time, DePAI protocols may ﬁnd that the greatest source of value is not selling data to third-party robotics companies, but developing 
proprietary physical AI models trained on data they alone can collect. While large-scale robotics data may take years or even decades to fully 
commoditize, demand for raw datasets is likely to decline as models become more capable and data eﬃciency improves. 
For that reason, it may be strategically rational for DePAI networks to begin building their own physical AI models early, using their proprietary 
data advantage rather than relying indeﬁnitely on data sales. This mirrors the broader verticalization trend across DePIN, where moving up the 
stack enables higher margins and more durable businesses. 
The long-term investment case for DePAI is therefore not limited to data collection. It lies in the development of diﬀerentiated physical AI models 
and operating systems built on exclusive, globally distributed physical data. 
The 2026 Catalyst: A Scarcity of TGEs Concentrating Attention in Select Tokens 
Demand for real-world data is accelerating as physical AI moves from research to deployment. At the same time, only a small number of 
purpose-built DePAI data collection networks exist, and most have not yet launched tokens. 
While existing DePIN networks demonstrate that demand for physical infrastructure is real, they are not optimized for robotics or embodied AI 
data. This creates a narrow window where the ﬁrst DePAI data collectors to launch tokens and validate revenue will stand largely alone as 
investable assets in the category. 
               
 


---

## Page 267

266 
In an environment where DeFi fees are compressing and speculative narratives are scarce, the launch of revenue-backed DePAI tokens could 
attract outsized attention. If Bitrobot, Prismax, or similar projects demonstrate even modest early revenue, it’s not unreasonable that capital would 
concentrate rapidly into a handful of tokens with extremely limited supply. 
Other projects such as OpenMind, Poseidon, Auki, peaq, and IoTeX may oﬀer broader exposure to the DePAI theme, but their adoption curves are 
likely to extend further into the future. 
Veriﬁed Onchain DePIN Revenue Surpasses $100 Million in 2026 
After a year of separating signal from noise, the DePIN sector now has a clearer understanding of where real, auditable economic value exists. 
While total revenue associated with DePIN activity likely exceeds $150 million annually, only a subset of that ﬁgure is veriﬁable onchain, a 
distinction that has become increasingly important to both investors and token holders. 
According to DePIN Pulse, onchain-veriﬁable DePIN revenue currently sits at roughly $50-$55 million annualized. While lower than commonly 
cited headline ﬁgures, this number represents a growing base of revenue that is transparent, auditable, and increasingly aligned with token 
economics. In practice, 2025 served as the sector’s “revenue validation” year, shifting the focus away from unaudited oﬀchain claims toward 
measurable onchain settlement. 
               
 


---

## Page 268

267 
 
Why Onchain Revenue Became the Benchmark 
Over the past cycle, inﬂated or opaque revenue ﬁgures, driven by oﬀchain settlement, intermediated partnerships, or unclear accounting, made it 
diﬃcult to assess true network traction or value accrual. As concerns with self dealing increased, the DePIN community increasingly converged on 
a simple standard: if revenue cannot be independently veriﬁed, it should not be considered. 
Messari aligns with this stance. Onchain-veriﬁable revenue provides a clean scoreboard for founders to optimize against and a credible metric for 
investors to underwrite growth. This is not a dismissal of oﬀchain revenue, much of it is real, but a recognition that markets cannot eﬃciently 
price what they cannot audit. 
Offchain Revenue Exists, but Attribution Remains Fragile 
               
 


---

## Page 269

268 
Several DePIN-adjacent businesses report substantial oﬀchain revenue. Grass indicated mid-eight-ﬁgure annual oﬀchain revenue in early 2025 
(now reporting much lower onchain revenues as of November), while Fuse reportedly generates $300 million in Annual Recurring Revenue 
(ARR) across its broader business. These ﬁgures are directionally important, but diﬃcult to attribute precisely to DePIN activity or to assess in 
terms of tokenholder value capture. In many cases, revenue is settled oﬀchain, bundled with non-DePIN services, or structured in ways that 
obscure its relationship to its native token. 
As a result, the key question is not whether DePIN generates revenue, it does, but whether that revenue is provable and structurally capable of 
ﬂowing onchain. 
Token Volatility Can Obfuscate Fundamentals Growth 
Because most DePINs receive payment for network usage in their native token, token volatility can draw attention away from fundamental growth. 
Protocols like Akash, DoubleZero, and Helium that saw a decline in token price over the year, yet saw strong revenue growth. As a result, the 
general market perception may be tainted by falling prices and revenues growing, creating increasingly attractive entry valuation as P/S ratios 
continue to decline. 
The signiﬁcance of obfuscated revenue growth is a potential breakout moment in 2026 where the market registers that top performing DePIN 
protocols may have even more attractive valuation than most TradFi equity counterparts. 
               
 


---

## Page 270

269 
 
Why Onchain DePIN Revenue Can Exceed $100 Million in 2026 
We expect 2026 to mark a step-change in onchain-veriﬁable DePIN revenue, as the groundwork laid over the past cycle begins to show up in 
reported numbers. The path to scale does not rely on aggressive assumptions and is driven by two primary vectors: 
● New TGEs launching with onchain-native revenue systems:Networks such as DAWN, BitRobot, and Daylight could settle revenue 
collected onchain in a timely manner, expanding the universe of revenue-producing DePIN tokens while improving measurability and 
transparency. 
● Expansion of existing networks:Established networks like Helium, Hivemapper, io.net, and Geodnet have already demonstrated real 
demand and are accelerating in revenue growth. From August 2025 to November 2025 Geodnet has grown from $3.9 million to $5.6 
million annualized, while Hivemapper has grown from $500,000 to $2.2 million annualized. We expect these incumbents to continue their 
growth, leading to a projected 2X in DePIN revenue onchain in 2026. 
Taken together, these dynamics create a credible trajectory for onchain DePIN revenue to grow from a ~$50 million run rate today to $100+ 
               
 


---

## Page 271

270 
million in 2026, even without assuming outsized growth from any single network. More importantly, this shift moves DePIN toward a standard of 
transparency and incentive alignment that markets can reliably price. 
InfraFi: Financing Net-New Infrastructure via Crypto Rails 
InfraFi will emerge as a breakout use case adjacent to DePIN, capturing demand for real-world, yield-bearing assets enabled by crypto while 
directly accelerating DePIN’s growth through capital formation synergies. 
At its core, InfraFi connects onchain capital to private infrastructure credit opportunities, oﬀering attractive, non-crypto-correlated yields to capital 
suppliers while ﬁlling persistent ﬁnancing gaps for select categories of infrastructure. Rather than funding speculative assets, InfraFi targets 
productive, cash-generating hardware that sits outside the reach of traditional capital markets. 
Why Onchain Private Credit Failed (So Far) 
Onchain private credit has yet to reach product-market ﬁt. Most early attempts have suﬀered from toxic ﬂow and adverse selection, where 
low-quality borrowers access traditional ﬁnancing and onchain pools are left underwriting inferior risk. 
Goldﬁnch is illustrative. Originally designed to use blockchain rails to eﬃciently extend credit to emerging markets, the protocol ultimately 
pivoted toward traditional corporate private credit. Despite the promise of lower costs and global access, underwriting proved insuﬃcient to 
protect investors, and the original thesis weakened. 
What’s Different This Time 
The InfraFi opportunity is not about reﬁnancing existing borrowers. It’s about ﬁnancing net-new assets created by structural shifts in the real 
economy. These assets generate novel ﬁnancing demand that traditional lenders are poorly positioned to initially serve. 
Two infrastructure categories stand out: 
● Compute. 
● Distributed Energy Resources (DERs). 
Both are experiencing explosive demand growth, capital intensity, and fragmentation, conditions that favor new ﬁnancing rails. 
Compute: Financing GPUs as Productive Assets 
On the compute front, USD.AI has emerged as the leading experiment in InfraFi, focusing on GPU ﬁnancing for AI startups. 
               
 


---

## Page 272

271 
 
Traditional private credit funds largely ignore this market. Their mandate favors large, proﬁtable loans, often with $20+ million minimums, 
extended to hyperscalers like CoreWeave that require billions in capital for large-scale data center deployments. Meanwhile, debt ﬁnancing is 
mostly unavailable for most AI startups. 
USD.AI targets this gap by ﬁnancing mid six-ﬁgure GPU purchases for startups that do not meet traditional thresholds. For these companies, debt 
ﬁnancing is often materially cheaper than equity ﬁnancing, particularly when compute costs can consume up to 80% of total expenditures. 
Financing GPUs with debt can therefore enable greater scale by lowering cost per unit of compute. 
Underwriting and Risk Mitigation 
The InfraFi thesis ultimately hinges on underwriting. Infrastructure credit fails when lenders cannot prevent fraud, misuse, or adverse selection, 
especially when the best borrowers have alternatives. 
               
 


---

## Page 273

272 
USD.AI attempts to address this through a combination of primitives and frameworks, including CALIBER, QEV, and FiLo. Most notable is its 
liquidation and custody model: 
● Borrowers never take physical possession of GPUs. 
● Hardware is delivered directly to a third-party data center and hosted on-site. 
● Borrowers gain usage rights, but no ownership or custody until the end of a three-year repayment term. 
In the event of default, USD.AI does not pursue legal claims. Instead, it repossesses the GPU in place and re-lends it to a new borrower without 
physical relocation. This transforms GPUs into reusable, income-generating assets that can be cycled through multiple credit relationships. 
Whether USD.AI can scale this model while maintaining underwriting discipline remains an open question. But the framework represents an 
intriguing evolution from prior onchain credit experiments. 
Energy: Financing Yield-Bearing DERs 
A parallel model is emerging in energy. Daylight’s DayFi applies similar InfraFi mechanics to ﬁnance yield-bearing electricity assets such as solar 
panels. These assets share many characteristics with compute: high upfront capex, predictable cash ﬂows, and growing demand driven by 
structural trends (powering generative AI, transition to clean energy, growing EV adoption). 
               
 


---

## Page 274

273 
 
An especially compelling frontier lies at the intersection of energy and compute, where power availability increasingly constrains AI deployment. 
As these two inputs become more tightly coupled, demand may emerge not only for ﬁnancing but also for derivative markets that hedge exposure 
to both electricity and compute pricing. 
Beyond Compute and Energy 
While compute and DERs are the clearest early candidates, InfraFi’s potential extends further. Within DePIN, telecom infrastructure, such as 
Helium hotspots or DAWN radio antenna systems, could beneﬁt from similar ﬁnancing models. 
Beyond DePIN, the design space expands further: satellites, EV ﬂeets, drone swarms, tourist rockets, and other capital-intensive systems where 
net-new assets generate cash ﬂows but fall outside traditional underwriting frameworks. 
               
 


---

## Page 275

274 
Bottom Line 
The InfraFi thesis is simple: 
Bootstrapping ﬁnancing for net-new, productive assets is faster and less costly onchain than building new ﬁnancial infrastructure from 
scratch. 
If crypto can reduce administrative friction, tap pre-built global capital pools, and improve capital market eﬃciency, InfraFi may prove to be one 
of the most durable real-world use cases adjacent to DePIN. 
The open question is not whether the demand exists for ﬁnancing, but whether crypto-native capital markets reduce costs and prove more eﬃcient 
compared to incumbents. 
Compute Derivative Markets Will Emerge Onchain First 
Building on the broader thesis that net-new assets and ﬁnancial use cases deploy more eﬃciently on crypto rails, compute derivatives stand out as 
one of the most compelling and underexplored opportunities. As compute become a core economic input for AI, cloud services, and digital 
infrastructure, there is still no mature global market for hedging compute price or availability risk. This gap creates a natural opening for 
crypto-native markets to lead. 
               
 


---

## Page 276

275 
 
Compute as a Net-New Financial Asset 
Compute, particularly GPU compute, is eﬀectively a new commodity. Unlike commodities such as oil or electricity, compute markets are 
fragmented, opaque, and subject to rapid technological change. Prices vary materially by chip type (e.g., H100 vs. A100), geography, contract 
duration, and availability. Supply chains are constrained, capex cycles are long, and demand is increasingly volatile. 
As a result, multiple market participants face signiﬁcant, unhedged risk: 
● Data center operators may want to lock in today’s price per GPU-hour to protect against future price declines as new supply comes online. 
● AI startups and enterprises may want to hedge against upward price pressure or shortages by ﬁxing long-term compute costs. 
● Traders and speculators may seek exposure to compute as a macro input into the AI economy. 
These dynamics mirror the early conditions that gave rise to energy and commodity derivatives, yet compute lacks the legacy market infrastructure 
               
 


---

## Page 277

276 
those assets beneﬁted from. 
Why Crypto Rails Are Better 
Crypto rails are uniquely well-suited to incubate compute derivative markets: 
● Liquidity is already present. Onchain perp and derivatives venues can bootstrap markets far faster than regulated, centralized counterparts. 
● Permissionless participation allows global data centers, startups, and traders to interact without bespoke legal or brokerage relationships. 
● Composability enables compute derivatives to plug directly into InfraFi, structured products, DePIN networks, and the broader crypto 
ecosystem. 
● New contract types (price, availability, utilization, chip-speciﬁc indices) can be launched with lower friction. 
By contrast, centralized markets face long lead times for regulatory approval, index construction, clearing infrastructure, and participant 
onboarding. By the time these markets form, crypto-native venues may already have established liquidity and pricing power. 
Beyond Price: Hedging Availability Risk 
Importantly, compute derivatives are not limited to price hedging. Availability risk may prove even more critical. For example, an AI company 
launching a new model may require guaranteed access to a ﬁxed number of H100 GPU-hours during a speciﬁc future window. A derivative 
contract tied to delivery or availability, rather than just spot price, could allow that ﬁrm to hedge execution risk, while compute suppliers monetize 
future capacity. 
These primitives blur the line between ﬁnancial derivatives and infrastructure markets, reinforcing synergies with DePIN and InfraFi. 
Early Players 
While still nascent, early data points suggest momentum: 
● Squaretower launched compute-linked perpetuals on Injective’s Helix in August, generating over $20 million in cumulative volume to date. 
● Ornn, which originated as a Web2 compute price index and marketplace, is signaling entry in Web3 infrastructure and has raised $5.8 
million, signaling growing investor interest in standardized compute pricing. 
● Global Compute Index’s also oﬀer compute perps based on compute price indices aggregated from a range of data sources. 
The most critical missing primitive remains a credible, manipulation-resistant compute price index. Without a trusted base truth for GPU pricing 
and availability, derivative markets struggle to scale. However, the incentives to build such indices increase rapidly should speculative and hedging 
demand materializes. 
Structural Tailwinds Into 2026 
               
 


---

## Page 278

277 
We believe compute derivatives are early but approaching an inﬂection point, with several powerful tailwinds: 
● Explosive demand growth: An estimated $5.2T in compute related capex is projected to be required by 2030. 
● Compute as a macro input: AI makes compute costs strategically important across industries. 
● Crypto-native speed: Permissionless capital and global liquidity dramatically compress time-to-market. 
● Deep synergies with DePIN and InfraFi: Financialization of infrastructure is a natural next step. 
Taken together, these factors suggest that compute derivatives are more likely to break out onchain ﬁrst, with crypto markets establishing a durable 
lead before centralized infrastructure can respond. If successful, this could represent one of the largest new ﬁnancial markets to emerge from 
crypto over the next cycle. 
The Time for Consumer Crypto is Now 
Authors: AJC and Austin Weiler 
Key Themes 
● The fee stack has ﬂipped from chains to apps. With blockspace no longer the bottleneck, consumer crypto is evolving into an 
application-led economy, where apps capture the majority of revenue and can ﬁnally optimize for user experience. 
● Consumer PMF is clearest where markets are the product. Memecoins/NFTs and prediction markets work because they embed ownership 
and pricing directly into cultural behavior and information-seeking, rather than bolting crypto onto existing apps. 
● Prediction markets graduated beyond elections into sustained usage. 2025 validated non-political demand (sports/crypto/culture), with 
distribution partnerships (e.g., Robinhood) acting as the major accelerant. 
● Financialized social is still in its early stages, but the design space is real. The opportunity isn’t decentralizing social; it’s making content, 
creators, and interactions tradable in a way that creates a net-new user experience. 
● Exotic RWAs are an emerging consumer wedge. Tokenization is starting to improve non-ﬁnancial goods markets (trading cards/gacha), 
with credible paths toward onchain liquidity, provenance, and composable ﬁnancial layers for collectibles. 
Introduction 
For years, large parts of the industry have approached consumer crypto from a philosophical standpoint. In the early days, perhaps that made 
sense. Bitcoin proved you could win by decentralizing money, so it wasn’t crazy to think you could win again by decentralizing Facebook, Uber, 
or Spotify. But with the beneﬁt of hindsight, it’s fair to say that this approach has largely been invalidated. Decentralization, censorship resistance, 
and self-sovereignty are important ideals, but the uncomfortable truth is that the average consumer simply does not care about them. No one is 
               
 


---

## Page 279

278 
leaving their favorite apps, starting from zero, and rebuilding their digital life just because the backend is “onchain.” 
What is hard to acknowledge, even for those of us who care about cypherpunk ideals, is that these principles aren’t what will unlock mainstream 
consumer adoption. And yet, from a purely practical standpoint, there has never been a better time to build consumer applications in crypto. 
 
In past cycles, high transaction costs made building an onchain consumer application an uphill battle. Blockchains captured the majority of fees, 
and every dollar that users spent on gas was, in essence, a tax on the consumer experience. 
However, over the past ﬁve years, onchain infrastructure has scaled greatly. Blockspace is no longer a bottleneck or a prohibitive cost. As a result, 
the fee landscape has undergone a dramatic shift. In 2021, blockchains made $13.51 billion in fees, accounting for 64% of all onchain revenue. In 
2025, blockchains generated just $2.43 billion, accounting for only 17% of onchain fees. Applications, not blockchains, now drive the majority of 
onchain revenue, a trend we expect to continue accelerating. 
Consumer crypto encompasses a wide range of applications, including memecoins, social networks, wallets, gaming, and more. And while it’s 
impossible to cover every subsector in depth, this year’s Theses will focus on the areas that have already found real product-market ﬁt, along with 
               
 


---

## Page 280

279 
the areas we believe are positioned to ﬁnd it next year and in the years ahead. 
Where Product-Market Fit is Today 
Memecoins and NFTs 
Consumer crypto’s oldest, and perhaps most well-known, products are NFTs and memecoins. While often dismissed as speculative distractions 
from “serious” use cases, these assets are some of the clearest examples of product-market ﬁt in crypto to date. They tap directly into cultural 
demand that already exists in the real world and bring it onchain through assets that users actively buy, trade, and rally around. 
 
The demand is undeniably cyclical, but when it materializes, it does so at a meaningful scale. In 2022, NFT and memecoin applications generated 
$2.11 billion in onchain fees, accounting for nearly 19% of all onchain fees. This cycle, we saw a similar trend, albeit at a slightly smaller scale. 
These applications generated $892.9 million in fees in 2024 (6% of total onchain fees) and $1.29 billion in 2025, representing 9% of all onchain 
               
 


---

## Page 281

280 
fees. Importantly, these ﬁgures only capture fees directly attributable to NFT and memecoin applications, and exclude fees paid to blockchains and 
intermediary venues, such as DEXs. In practice, the total onchain economic activity driven by NFTs and memecoins is signiﬁcantly higher. 
Memecoins and NFTs are probably the clearest expression of crypto’s cultural value. In the real world, we already assign a premium to select 
assets with no fundamental cash ﬂows, such as jewelry, watches, art, sneakers, Funko Pops, and even plush toys like Labubu. None of these 
produces income or solves a hard economic problem, but they have cultural value through status, identity, nostalgia, and taste. 
Memecoins and NFTs fall into the same category. They might not have discounted cash ﬂows or clear utility, but that doesn’t mean they’re 
worthless. Their value comes from shared narratives, in-jokes, communities, and online identity. Some memecoins ﬁt this framing far better than 
others. Tokens like SPX and MOG, which have spawned persistent, cult-like communities, align neatly with this idea. In contrast, memecoins tied 
to one-oﬀ viral moments, like PWEASE, do not. For the remainder of this section, we refer to memecoins in the former category. 
In this sense, memecoins and NFTs serve a surprisingly important role, as they demonstrate how society assigns cultural value to crypto. When 
these assets trend down only, it functions as a canary in the coal mine, signaling that the foundational ideas that shaped crypto may not be 
resonating as strongly as they once did. Unfortunately, the cultural value of crypto appears to be lower now than at any point in recent memory. 
               
 


---

## Page 282

281 
 
NFTs are now entering their fourth year of a bear market, following a peak in late 2021 and early 2022. The total market cap of NFTs has 
decreased by 63% in 2025 alone, currently standing at $3.00 billion. The decline is more pronounced when examining individual collections. 
Milady, which even received public support from Ethereum co-founder Vitalik Buterin earlier this year, is down 75%, with its market cap now at 
$34.8 million. The only slight bright spot has been CryptoPunks, which are down a comparatively modest 28%, propped up in part by 
PunkStrategy, a protocol that algorithmically buys and sells Punks using trading fees. 
               
 


---

## Page 283

282 
 
Memecoins have not fared any better. The memecoin euphoria of 2024 has come to an end, and prices have collapsed across the board. The total 
memecoin market cap is down 59% in 2025, currently standing at $39.06 billion (BTC is down 3% over the same period). WIF, the token that 
arguably kicked oﬀ the “Memecoin Supercycle,” is among the hardest hit, down 80% this year. Even one of the few memecoins that broke into the 
spotlight in 2025, FARTCOIN, is down 66% on the year. 
The simplest explanation for the collapse in memecoins is that the game got ﬁgured out, leading to a classic speculative bust. And yes, that 
dynamic played a role. But rather than eulogizing the category, it’s more constructive to ask how memecoins and NFTs can be improved. Both 
have tapped into real cultural demand in the past, so the challenge now is ﬁguring out how to reignite it. 
               
 


---

## Page 284

283 
 
The ﬁrst key insight for this sector is that memecoins and NFTs are two sides of the same coin; both are expressions of crypto’s cultural value. As 
a result, they largely compete for the same pool of capital and attention. Up until early 2024, capital was split roughly 50/50 between memecoins 
(excluding DOGE) and NFTs. However, once memecoins truly took oﬀ in Q1'24, the balance shifted dramatically, and the split has hovered closer 
to 80/20 ever since. 
               
 


---

## Page 285

284 
 
Ultimately, memecoins and NFTs competing against each other end up hurting both. They draw liquidity, attention, and buyers away from one 
another instead of reinforcing the same ecosystem. The clearest example of this came from the wave of NFT collections that launched their own 
tokens at the end of last year: Milady & CULT, Pudgy Penguins & PENGU, and Azuki & ANIME. 
The outcome of their token launches, for lack of a better word, was brutal. Not only did the tokens fail to retain their value, but the underlying 
NFTs also experienced a signiﬁcant decline in value. From their respective token launches: 
● Milady: -86% 
● CULT: -96% 
● Pudgy Penguins: -87% 
● PENGU: -61% 
● Azuki: -92% 
● ANIME: -93% 
Instead of creating new demand, these token launches siphoned liquidity out of their own ecosystems, weakening both the NFT and token sides of 
               
 


---

## Page 286

285 
the brand. 
The ﬁrst step toward recovery in crypto’s cultural sector is addressing the structural divide between memecoins and NFTs. Right now, they 
fracture the very demand they’re supposed to capture. Take a user who wants exposure to Remilia. What are they supposed to buy? A Milady? 
CULT? A secondary collection like Redacted Remilio Babies? 
Even if they pick one, there’s no guarantee they’re actually getting exposure to the Remilia community in the way they intend. Buying CULT 
doesn’t lift Milady prices, and buying a Milady doesn’t aﬀect CULT. The ecosystem is split across multiple assets that don’t reinforce each other. 
If Remilia becomes culturally relevant, but that relevance is only reﬂected in the token, Milady holders miss out on the upside. If it appears only in 
the NFT, CULT holders miss out on the upside. 
The reverse dynamic has also played out. Once a memecoin gains real cultural traction, an accompanying NFT drop is almost guaranteed, diluting 
attention and liquidity yet again. 
 
The core problem with today’s cultural assets is simple. NFTs and memecoins split exposure. Communities want one thing to rally around, but 
               
 


---

## Page 287

286 
instead they’re forced into a menu of disconnected assets: an NFT, a token, a secondary collection, a derivative drop, none of which reinforce each 
other. ERC-404 is a potential solution to this problem. 
ERC-404 is a hybrid token standard that merges the liquidity of fungible tokens with the uniqueness of NFTs. By doing so, it directly addresses 
the issue of fragmentation. Instead of issuing a separate token and hoping it doesn’t cannibalize the NFT, ERC-404 ties the two together in a 
single asset. Fractional amounts trade like a token on AMMs (giving you liquidity), but holding one full unit corresponds to an NFT (giving you 
cultural expression, identity, and status). 
For example, using ERC-404, a Remilia-style ecosystem wouldn’t need separate assets for CULT, Milady, and Remilio Babies. Instead, there 
would be one uniﬁed asset. If the brand becomes culturally relevant, both the liquid token and the NFT expression capture that value 
simultaneously, because they are the same asset. In an ERC-404 model, you don’t get dilution across multiple assets, you don’t get narratives 
pulling in diﬀerent directions, and you don’t have to guess which instrument will actually capture the upside. By unifying liquidity and cultural 
expression into a single asset, ERC-20 resolves the tension between memecoins and NFTs rather than attempting to balance them through separate 
instruments. 
ERC-404 may be able to address the market structure of NFTs and memecoins, but it will not resolve the deeper issue plaguing these assets: their 
lack of cultural appeal. In retrospect, the launch of TRUMP and the vampire attack by MELANIA just days later severely damaged the credibility 
of crypto’s culture. The TRUMP memecoin was already pushing the limits, but the MELANIA launch exposed what the memecoin sector had 
eﬀectively become: a cash-grab opportunity. Kerosene was then thrown onto an already burning ﬂame with the subsequent launches of LIBRA, 
YZY, and countless other memecoins that served no purpose beyond extracting money for their creators. 
At this point, it is hard to argue that the cultural value of this asset sector is not completely in the gutter. If you disagree, try to ﬁnd a memecoin or 
NFT with a market cap above $1 million that is also up year-over-year (Good luck!). The road to recovery will be long, and we’re not exactly 
hopeful it will happen in 2026, but, a recovery will happen… eventually. 
That recovery will not be driven by fundamentals, utility, or technological breakthroughs. It will happen because memecoins and NFTs remain the 
most eﬀective vehicles for expressing shared, collective belief in the social value of an asset. As long as humans continue to speculate on cultural 
meaning, a practice they have engaged in for centuries, the appetite to assign and trade social value will not disappear. When that speculative 
impulse inevitably returns onchain, it will once again ﬂow into memecoins and NFTs. The hope is that, when it does, the market is built on more 
resilient structures, potentially through standards like ERC-404, rather than the extractive models that deﬁned the most recent cycle. 
Prediction Markets 
Prediction markets broke into the mainstream during the 2024 U.S. Presidential Election as Polymarket and Kalshi odds appeared alongside 
traditional polling. Their markets were viewed as an alternative barometer of electoral sentiment and ultimately proved more eﬀective in 
predicting the eventual election outcome than conventional polls. 
               
 


---

## Page 288

287 
 
In the ﬁve months leading up to the election, Polymarket and Kalshi volume grew 3,186% from $140.0 million in May 2024 to $4.6 billion in 
October 2024, the peak month before the November 5 election. This surge made prediction markets one of the ﬁrst breakout applications in 
crypto. 
However, political markets accounted for 62% of prediction market volume in 2024, leading many to view politics as the only real use case and 
question whether demand could persist beyond U.S. election cycles. 
Initially, skeptics were proven right as monthly volume fell 63% over the four months following the election, from $4.6 billion in October 2024 to 
$1.7 billion in February 2025. 
However, during the rest of 2025, prediction markets resoundingly proved they have clear PMF beyond political markets. 
After the February low, monthly volume on Polymarket and Kalshi increased 441% to $9.2 billion in November, with September, October, and 
November 2025 all surpassing the previous October 2024 highs. 
This acceleration stemmed from non-political markets, including sports, crypto, and culture. From July to December 2024, non-political markets 
               
 


---

## Page 289

288 
accounted for 38% ($6.0 billion) of the volume on Polymarket and Kalshi. From January to November 2025, non-political markets accounted for 
80% ($31.1 billion) of the volume across the two platforms. Prediction markets expanded signiﬁcantly beyond election-driven demand to achieve 
sustained, non-political usage. 
 
In 2025, the sports sector drove the majority of growth in prediction market volumes. From January to November, the sports sector led volume 
with a 58% share ($23.1 billion). Over the same period, the political sector ranked second with a 20% share ($7.8 billion), followed by the crypto 
sector in third with an 11% share ($4.5 billion), and the culture sector in fourth with a 3% share ($1.2 billion). 
The catalyst that propelled the sports sector forward was Kalshi’s partnership with Robinhood on August 19, which enabled users to trade NFL 
and college football markets through the Robinhood Prediction Markets Hub. The partnership had a twofold impact. First, the platform reduced 
friction for non-crypto-native users by enabling them to trade through their existing Robinhood accounts. Second, it provided U.S. users a 
regulated path to trade sports outcomes with better odds than traditional sportsbooks like DraftKings and FanDuel. Following the partnership, the 
               
 


---

## Page 290

289 
monthly sports sector volume increased by 551% from $965.2 million in August to $6.3 billion in November. 
Despite strong momentum in 2025, volumes on prediction markets still only account for a small portion of the broader sports betting landscape. In 
2024, U.S.-licensed sportsbooks processed $150 billion in betting volume, with FanDuel handling $50.7 billion and DraftKings handling $49.4 
billion. 
One factor that largely explains why prediction markets still trail traditional sportsbooks in sports betting volume is the limited wager types, 
speciﬁcally parlay bets and player props. Polymarket does not support parlays, while Kalshi oﬀers limited parlay functionality. Additionally, both 
platforms provide minimal player props. That limitation matters because parlays account for an estimated 30% of traditional sportsbook volume, 
driven by their higher implied payouts and appeal to retail bettors. Without robust parlay and prop oﬀerings, prediction markets leave a 
meaningful portion of sports betting demand unaddressed. 
We believe expanding beyond straight bets represents a clear opportunity to close that gap and should be a focus for prediction markets in 2026. 
Even with those constraints, prediction markets compete where it matters most: pricing. Their orderbook-based structure allows users to trade 
against each other, rather than the “house,” resulting in tighter odds and higher expected payouts for the same outcome. That advantage 
compounds for whales, who place large wagers, where small improvements in odds signiﬁcantly aﬀect their returns. In 2026, we expect this 
pricing edge to continue drawing users away from traditional sportsbooks, particularly larger bettors, and drive further growth in prediction market 
sports volume. 
While sports dominated volume, culture became the fastest-growing prediction market sector in the latter half of 2025. From August to November, 
monthly culture volume grew 625% from $43.6 million to $316.1 million. The increase stemmed from sustained activity across many cultural 
markets, rather than a single headline event. 
Culture markets matter for two reasons. First, the sector posted the second-highest volume-to-open-interest ratio across sectors, trailing only the 
sports sector, which signals high turnover and frequent resolution. That behavior favors platforms that monetize transaction volume, since users 
recycle capital rather than locking it in long-dated bets. 
Second, culture markets have no real alternatives. Sports markets compete with sportsbooks, but no equivalent venue exists for trading outcomes 
tied to internet culture, entertainment, or public social sentiment (i.e., What will be the top Netﬂix show this week?). Prediction markets are the 
only place where users can both create and trade on these outcomes. This mirrors political prediction markets in 2024, where the absence of 
viable alternatives concentrated activity and drove rapid volume expansion. 
That structural advantage gives culture markets a clear path to sustained adoption as prediction markets expand beyond their early user base. 
Kalshi CEO Tarek Mansour has said that culture markets have the most growth potential of any prediction market sector over the next ﬁve years. 
As prediction markets permeate non-crypto-native audiences, they will naturally reach users with cultural expertise. Once those users recognize 
that prediction markets let them trade on that knowledge, they will gravitate to the only venue where it is monetizable. Together, these factors 
position culture to rank among the top three fastest-growing prediction market sectors by volume in 2026. 
               
 


---

## Page 291

290 
 
In 2025, prediction market open interest (OI) was a two-horse race between Polymarket and Kalshi, which together accounted for a 91% ($627.7 
million) share of the market. From June 1 to November 30, Kalshi OI grew 258% from $93.7 million to $335.3 million. Over the same period, 
Polymarket OI grew 133% from $125.3 million to $292.4 million. The gap between the two remained narrow throughout the year, but both 
platforms pulled meaningfully ahead of smaller competitors. 
That OI expansion coincided with a year of aggressive ecosystem building. In 2025, both platforms expanded distribution through partnerships 
with major brands, including CNN, CNBC, UFC, NHL, and Yahoo Finance, which are expected to increase mainstream exposure. At the same 
time, both companies raised signiﬁcant capital. Polymarket raised three rounds during the year, capped on October 7 by a $2 billion investment 
from ICE, the parent company of the NYSE, valuing the company at $9 billion. Kalshi raised two rounds, led by a $1 billion undisclosed funding 
round on November 19, which valued the company at $11 billion. 
Taken together, rising OI, expanded distribution, and fresh capital in 2025 position both Polymarket and Kalshi to sustain their current pace of 
growth into 2026, even before factoring in additional product launches or incentive programs. 
               
 


---

## Page 292

291 
In the second half of 2025, Polymarket worked toward the launch of its U.S. app, which went live on December 3 for waitlisted users. The public 
rollout represents a major distribution unlock that we expect to materially increase Polymarket’s OI and volume in 2026. Kalshi’s OI and volume 
rose sharply after its partnership with Robinhood in August, which expanded access to non-crypto-native users. If Polymarket’s U.S. app follows a 
similar adoption curve once broadly available, we expect it to result in a signiﬁcant increase in both OI and volume. 
A second catalyst that sits alongside distribution is a potential airdrop. On October 24, Polymarket CMO Matthew Modabber conﬁrmed plans for 
a POLY token and a future airdrop. Although the timing remains unconﬁrmed, market expectations suggest a 2026 launch. Combined with a fully 
available U.S. app, the airdrop introduces an additional incentive mechanism that Kalshi does not currently match. If both catalysts materialize in 
2026, Polymarket’s OI growth will accelerate ahead of Kalshi and pull away from its closest competitor. 
For most of 2025, no prediction market platform outside of Polymarket and Kalshi made meaningful progress on OI until Opinion entered the 
picture. Opinion launched its prediction market, Opinion.Trade, on October 24, on BNB Chain and reached $63.2 million in OI. Prior to Opinion’s 
launch, no other prediction market platform beyond Polymarket and Kalshi had surpassed $3 million in OI, which made Opinion’s early traction 
stand out. 
Opinion did not mirror existing platforms as it launched the ﬁrst prediction market native to BNB Chain, and with a diﬀerentiated product, 
Opinion AI. Opinion AI is a market-creation tool that turns simple prompts into fully speciﬁed Yes/No markets with clear resolution rules, 
allowing users to create markets faster than on competing platforms. In terms of OI and volume, Opinion has already distinguished itself from 
long-tail crypto-native competitors, such as Limitless and Myriad. By combining a diﬀerentiated market-creation product with access to the BNB 
Chain user base, Opinion carved out a credible path to third place by the end of 2025. In 2026, we believe it can be one of the best-performing 
crypto-native alternatives to Polymarket and Kalshi. 
Competition will also intensify from incumbent sportsbooks outside the crypto sector. In 2026, both DraftKings and FanDuel are expected to 
expand into prediction markets, primarily to reach users in states where traditional sports betting remains illegal, such as California and Texas, and 
to oﬀer non-sports markets, including political and macroeconomic outcomes. DraftKings plans to launch DraftKings Predictions in Q1 2026 
following its acquisition of Railbird, a CFTC-licensed exchange. FanDuel has discussed a similar strategy, positioning prediction markets as 
complementary to its sportsbook by enabling trading on events such as elections and oil prices. 
In these macro and non-sports categories, incumbents hold a clear distribution advantage, and we expect them to take market share in 2026, 
speciﬁcally in markets their users previously could not access. DraftKings and FanDuel already dominate sports betting volume, so launching 
prediction markets is unlikely to signiﬁcantly expand their share within sports. The impact is more meaningful in non-sports markets, where 
crypto-native prediction markets previously beneﬁted from being the only venues oﬀering easily accessible markets such as FOMC rate decisions. 
As sportsbooks launch comparable prediction markets, that exclusivity evaporates for the largest and most liquid non-sports markets. However, we 
believe crypto-native prediction markets will retain an advantage in market diversity and long-tail coverage, which will preserve their activity even 
as incumbents compete for headline markets. 
               
 


---

## Page 293

292 
Ultimately, despite increased competition from both crypto-native prediction markets and emerging challengers from incumbent sportsbooks, we 
believe Polymarket and Kalshi will remain the clear leaders in the prediction market space. Polymarket could pull ahead of Kalshi if it 
successfully executes a public U.S. app launch, token launch, and potential airdrop. Regardless, both platforms possess the brand recognition and 
capital resources to remain the leading players in prediction markets for the foreseeable future. 
Future PMF through Markets 
We believe the most compelling value proposition of consumer crypto is its ability to embed markets directly into consumer experiences. Rather 
than treating pricing and ownership as abstract or hidden layers, crypto makes them native to the product itself. In practice, this occurs in two 
ways: 
1. Creating markets where none previously existed. 
2. Improving markets in existing consumer experiences that are currently burdened by friction. 
Many of the clearest examples of product-market ﬁt in consumer crypto already follow this pattern. Memecoins and NFTs embed markets into 
internet communities, allowing collective attention and identity to be expressed through price. Prediction markets apply the same logic, replacing 
polls and pundits with tradable probabilities. In each case, markets are not an accessory to the product; they are the product. 
This framework extends naturally beyond crypto-native assets. Consumer crypto can make implicit value explicit by pricing things that were 
previously unpriced, and it can take existing markets and rebuild them onchain in ways that reduce friction, improve transparency, and expand 
what users can do. Where consumer behavior already exists, crypto’s advantage is oﬀering a better way to interact with it. 
The white whale of consumer crypto has always been social media. The dominant platforms (Facebook, TikTok, YouTube, etc.) demonstrate that 
social networks occupy the top of the value stack in consumer tech. If a social platform built on crypto rails actually works at scale, the upside is 
measured in hundreds of billions, not millions. 
Because of that opportunity, there have been repeated attempts over the years to build “crypto’s social platform.” Some have caught lightning in a 
bottle (BitClout in 2021, Friend.tech in 2023, Farcaster in 2024), but none have achieved lasting traction. As a result, social has become one of the 
most polarizing sectors in crypto. While the opportunity is clear, many argue that the network eﬀects established by incumbents have created truly 
impenetrable moats. 
In past Theses, we’ve talked about DeSoc from a philosophical standpoint, such as how social media needs to be decentralized to protect users 
from censorship. This year, we’re taking a more practical approach and retiring the DeSoc term entirely. For a crypto-based social platform to 
succeed, it needs to oﬀer a net-new experience for users, not just replace the backend infrastructure with crypto primitives. And this isn’t just our 
view, Farcaster’s Dan Romero said outright in “State of Farcaster, December 2025,” that decentralization hasn’t delivered PMF. 
               
 


---

## Page 294

293 
 
Zooming out, we still believe there’s a real opportunity for a crypto social platform to succeed. The amount of time society spends online 
continues to increase, and so does the number of platforms people use. In 2010, only ﬁve social platforms had more than 100 million monthly 
active users. By 2015, that number had grown to 19, and by 2025, it reached 34. A crypto social platform doesn’t need to replace an existing social 
primitive; it just needs to be additive to a consumer’s expanding set of online behaviors. 
A crypto social media platform’s greatest strength will be its ability to fully ﬁnancialize the social experience. Traditional platforms have already 
been inching in this direction to support the massive creator economy, which is expected to reach $480 billion by 2027. X creator payouts, 
YouTube revenue sharing, and TikTok’s branded-content marketplace are all ways for social platforms to plug into creator monetization. 
Furthermore, the creator economy exists because online content has real value. For 99.99% of posts, that value rounds down to zero, but in 
aggregate, the stream of content created every day is enormously valuable, hence the half-trillion-dollar creator economy. The problem is that this 
value is largely hidden. Each post has a price, but traditional platforms keep that price hidden from both creators and users. 
Herein lies the edge for ﬁnancialized social media. Not only can crypto move creator payouts onchain, but it can make the value of content public 
by turning posts, creators, and interactions into open markets. Creating markets around social content is the zero-to-one moment for crypto social 
               
 


---

## Page 295

294 
platforms. 
All of this brings us to the projects that are actually making progress in this direction. In 2025, the two clear frontrunners are pump.fun and Zora. 
Pump.fun 
Pump.fun has long dominated the launchpad space, and it’s now trying to leverage that position to expand into a full-ﬂedged social platform. 
When the team announced their token earlier this year, they made their ambition explicit: “Kill Facebook, TikTok, and Twitch. On Solana.” 
At ﬁrst, pump.fun’s go-to-market strategy centered heavily on streaming. They claim that their creator-earnings model, Project Ascend, oﬀers 
streamers a far more compelling way to monetize than traditional platforms by allowing them to earn directly from trading fees. Combine that 
with pump.fun’s degenerate user base, which is always ready to speculate on almost anything, and you have the ingredients for a strong 
onboarding funnel for streamers. 
 
Initially, this strategy proved successful for pump.fun. On September 14, Bagwork, an upstart streaming duo, captured attention across crypto and 
mainstream media with a mix of outrageous stunts, including streaking at football games, getting tattoos at market cap milestones, and leaking 
               
 


---

## Page 296

295 
unreleased music from rapper Drake. Their streams generated massive attention and netted them $289,400 in creator fees. The virality of 
Bagwork, along with the amount of money they made streaming, catalyzed a surge in streamers on pump.fun. In the week leading up to 
September 14, pump.fun averaged around 9,000 creators claiming fees. In the following week, pump.fun averaged 15,500. 
However, this surge in streaming on pump.fun was short-lived. In November, only an average of 6,700 creators claimed fees, and almost none of 
these creators were streamers. As of writing, there are 157 streamers live on pump.fun. Comparatively, there are 121,900 streamers live on Twitch, 
33,800 on YouTube, and 13,300 on Kick. 
With streaming growth stalling out, pump.fun has started shifting its focus elsewhere. On October 31, the team announced Spotlight, a new 
initiative aimed at accelerating Internet Capital Markets (ICM) on pump.fun. 
Zora 
The other major competitor in the social space is Zora. Earlier this year, Zora completely overhauled its protocol, abandoning its L2 and legacy 
NFT products in favor of moving to Base and fully embracing tokenization. On Zora, every account and every post becomes a token, meaning that 
every piece of content is tradable by default. This creates a fundamentally diﬀerent social experience where the user’s feed doubles as a curated 
list of markets.Through this model, Zora unlocks two key net new user experiences. First, every single piece of content a creator publishes 
becomes a monetization opportunity, since they earn a share of trading fees whenever someone buys their post. Although many platforms already
