help creators earn money, Zora improves upon existing models by turning every post into a potential revenue stream, not just long-form videos or 
sponsorship deals. 
Second, instead of being passive likers, viewers, or retweeters, users can actually take a position on the content they think will take oﬀ. If a post 
goes viral, early buyers win alongside the creator. It turns social engagement into something you can participate in, not just observe, a loop where 
attention, belief, and capital all feed into each other. 
               
 


---

## Page 297

296 
 
Zora has shown strong momentum in 2025. Usage has climbed meaningfully throughout the year, with growth concentrated around a few major 
onboarding waves. In June, Zora averaged 1,800 daily unique creators and 5,500 coins created per day. By late July and early August, during its 
ﬁrst real breakout moment, those numbers surged to 18,200 daily creators (up 921% from June) and 43,400 coins created per day (up 697%). 
Activity naturally cooled from those peaks, but the reset still landed far above where the platform started. In November, Zora averaged 13,300 
daily unique creators and 34,800 coins created each day, levels that point to real retention and a steadily growing user base. Even if the spikes 
weren’t fully sustainable, Zora translated them into a durable foundation of consistent users. 
Solving for the Demand Side 
In the grand scheme of things, both pump.fun and Zora are still small players in the social media landscape. Pump.fun has only been able to attract 
a few hundred streamers, and Zora’s user base is measured in the thousands, a rounding error compared to traditional platforms with tens or 
hundreds of millions of users. This gap reﬂects unresolved constraints in how these platforms generate sustained demand around social assets. 
Despite recent momentum, pump.fun and Zora run into those constraints in diﬀerent ways. On pump.fun, the challenge is internal. Its existing 
user base is highly active, yet largely indiﬀerent to streamer coins. Traders show little willingness to buy, hold, or repeatedly trade tokens tied to 
               
 


---

## Page 298

297 
individual creators, particularly when those tokens lack a clear connection to the creator’s ongoing success. 
Zora’s problem is external. Although its creator and content coins have a more compelling market structure than pump.fun’s streamer coins, the 
platform has not yet attracted a large user base that shows up speciﬁcally to trade them. As a result, many assets are created, but few sustain 
meaningful liquidity or repeat engagement. 
For both pump.fun and Zora, improving the user experience requires making social assets worth engaging with beyond a single trade. Social 
tokens become more compelling when ownership unlocks concrete actions, access, interaction, prediction, or routing user spending, such as tips, 
subscriptions, or advertising back through the asset itself. Importantly, Zora has already begun moving in this direction with features like 
token-gated direct messaging. 
Future Outlook 
These challenges are not a reason for despair. Both pump.fun and Zora are early, and their shortcomings point to design problems that are solvable 
rather than structural dead ends. Financialized social media remains an underexplored surface area, and even modest improvements in how users 
engage with social assets could unlock signiﬁcant growth from today’s small base. 
At this stage, however, we are far more bullish on Zora’s social growth prospects than pump.fun’s. This is not a knock on pump.fun; the platform 
has built a massive and highly active user base. The issue is one of intent. Pump.fun users primarily show up to speculate on memecoins and new 
launches, rather than developing durable relationships with individual creators or streamers. As a result, social features struggle to gain lasting 
traction. 
In that context, it likely makes more sense for pump.fun to double down on its core product rather than force a social layer onto a user base that 
has not shown sustained demand for it. Recent moves such as Spotlight and the acquisition of the trading terminal Padre may already signal this 
strategic shift. 
Zora, on the other hand, enters 2026 with far more favorable tailwinds. First and foremost, Coinbase appears to be all in on the idea that crypto 
can reshape social media and the creator economy. They’ve completely reworked Coinbase Wallet into the Base App, with a strong emphasis on 
social features. The app integrates directly with crypto-native social platforms like Zora and Farcaster, and the consistent marketing message has 
been simple: help creators earn. As the largest crypto company in America, Coinbase gives Zora an unrivaled distribution advantage, arguably the 
single most important ingredient for scaling a new social platform. 
Another major tailwind for Zora is speculation around the upcoming BASE token. In September, Base conﬁrmed that it is “exploring” the launch 
of a native token for Base. Although no further details have been announced, it is not hard to imagine Base using the token to incentivize activity 
around the Base app, including Zora. 
Zora’s ﬁnal, and perhaps most important, advantage over pump.fun lies in its monetary model. Pump.fun relies on SOL as its monetary asset, with 
both the platform and creators monetizing almost exclusively through trading fees. This structure implicitly rewards volatility and churn. Coins 
that spike, collapse, and generate high turnover are more proﬁtable for the platform and creators than coins that compound in value and reward 
               
 


---

## Page 299

298 
long-term holders, leaving trader outcomes largely unaligned with platform incentives. 
Zora addresses this mismatch by adopting an application money model. By using ZORA as the base monetary asset, value created on the platform 
is internalized rather than leaked to an external settlement layer. As activity increases, demand accrues to ZORA, aligning creators, users, and 
traders around the same outcome: a stronger base asset. In this model, the success of individual creator/content coins reinforces the health of the 
broader ecosystem, rather than existing as isolated fee-generating events (see “Cryptomoney Is the Foundation of the Industry” for a deeper 
discussion). 
 
Zora’s application money model is already showing early signs of working in practice. Because all creator and content coin liquidity is routed 
through Uniswap V4’s singleton contract, growth on Zora can be approximated by tracking how much ZORA is deposited into Uniswap V4. 
ZORA deposits in Uniswap V4 have trended upwards throughout the entire year, despite signiﬁcant volatility surrounding the ZORA token. 
Deposits have surpassed 121.5 million ZORA (equivalent to $5.9 million), a 66x increase over the last six months. Beneath the noise, this is the 
               
 


---

## Page 300

299 
clearest indication that Zora is ﬁnding early PMF with a subset of creators and users, positioning it well into 2026. 
Exotic RWAs 
One of the biggest trends outside of crypto in 2025 has been the surging popularity of Pokémon, trading card games (TCGs), and sports cards. 
These products have rapidly expanded from niche hobbies into a thriving multibillion-dollar industry. Market Decipher estimates the sports 
trading card market at $14.9 billion, while Zion Market Research values the trading card game market at $7.4 billion, together suggesting a 
combined market of over $22 billion. 
 
Beyond headline estimates, the surge in demand reveals itself in secondary market prices for popular cards. For example, the average price of an 
ungraded Mew Ex #232, one of the more sought-after cards within the industry, has increased 360% since January 2024, from $112 to $516. This 
is just one card, but it illustrates the signiﬁcant new demand that has entered the space. 
With trading cards and collectibles breaking into the mainstream, crypto has an opportunity to solve fundamental pain points (or ineﬃciencies) in 
               
 


---

## Page 301

300 
these markets through tokenization. And we’re already seeing it happen. A good example is the rise of onchain gacha-style pack openings. For 
more than a century, collectors have opened packs in the same way: you buy a sealed pack, rip it open, and hope for a hit. In 2025, onchain 
marketplaces like Courtyard, Collector Crypt, Phygitals, Beezie, Emporium, and Rip.fun took that same idea and rebuilt it on blockchain rails. 
These platforms ship physical trading cards to secure vaults and issue tradeable NFTs that can be redeemed for the underlying card. The main 
driver of their activity has been the Gacha-style mechanics, where users purchase randomized “sealed” packs of tokenized cards, which can then 
be digitally “ripped” to reveal the cards within the pack. Unlike traditional Gacha systems, which are constrained by slow, manual card shipments 
through illiquid secondary markets, onchain implementations oﬀer near-instant liquidity as marketplaces provide buyback mechanisms that return 
80%-90% of a card’s value immediately. 
 
Onchain gacha is clearly ﬁnding strong PMF. In November, the top six marketplaces facilitated $62.2 million in volume, up from $10.4 million in 
January, representing a 497% increase over the previous eleven months. At the current pace, onchain gachas are on track to clear over $600 
million in volume in 2025. For reference, GameStop’s “Collectibles” segment generated $439.1 million in the ﬁrst half of 2025 ($878.2 million 
               
 


---

## Page 302

301 
annualized). 
The comparison isn’t one-to-one—gacha platforms earn more per unit of inventory, and GameStop has a broader product lineup—but it still 
highlights how fast onchain gachas have scaled. A year ago, most of these platforms were relatively unknown. Now, they’re handling tens of 
millions of dollars in monthly volume and demonstrating that there is real demand for digital-native ways to interact with physical collectibles. 
This is just one example of a much broader shift starting to take shape. Onchain gacha and tokenized trading cards are likely just the ﬁrst iteration 
of what we refer to as “Exotic Real-World Assets (RWAs).” Exotic RWAs are tokenized representations of goods or assets that are not inherently 
ﬁnancial instruments. While trading cards are the most prominent example today, the category also encompasses fashion items, luxury goods, and 
other collectibles. These asset classes face structural frictions that tokenization can help mitigate, such as reliance on intermediaries, high shipping 
and insurance costs, and fragmented grading and resale workﬂows. 
The ﬁrst wave of adoption has come from onchain gacha, but the larger opportunity lies in bringing the entire collectibles stack onchain. This 
could include grading and authentication recorded immutably onchain, permissionless appraisals backed by economic stake to discourage fraud, 
custody arrangements where ownership transfers without requiring physical movement of the asset, and more. Over time, secondary trading, 
insurance, lending, and dispute resolution could also be natively integrated, reducing reliance on intermediaries and enabling more liquid, 
transparent, and composable markets for non-ﬁnancial goods. If successful, Exotic RWAs could emerge as an asset class that is easier to trade, 
easier to collateralize, and more liquid than traditional collectibles. 
For 2026, we expect onchain gacha platforms to continue leading the exotic RWA sector, driving additional volume and bringing more trading 
cards onchain. Beyond trading cards, other exotic RWAs may also begin to gain traction as infrastructure matures and user familiarity increases. 
Some early examples include Baxus, a marketplace for tokenized whiskey and spirits; Fitted, which focuses on clothing and fashion items; Huch, 
a marketplace for tokenized CS:GO skins; and House Protocol, which is positioning itself as an onchain alternative to eBay. While still early, 
these platforms illustrate the expanding scope of exotic RWAs beyond trading cards. 
Taken together, exotic RWAs represent one of the more promising and underexplored opportunities in the consumer crypto space. As collectibles 
and adjacent consumer goods continue to grow in cultural relevance and economic value, tokenization oﬀers a path to materially improve 
liquidity, transparency, and market access in asset classes that have historically been fragmented and ineﬃcient. 
Disruption Factor: A Proof-of-Concept 
Framework for Evaluating L2s 
Crypto has never suﬀered from a shortage of activity. New chains, new tokens, new narratives - every cycle brings an explosion of innovation and 
noise. However, one question has remained stubbornly diﬃcult to answer: Which projects truly have the chance to make a lasting impact? 
               
 


---

## Page 303

302 
Throughout Messari’s history, we’ve applied the best-available frameworks, from traditional valuation thinking to network and market-structure 
models, in search of a reliable, concise way to evaluate projects. Each time, the same ﬂaw surfaced: protocols do not win the same way traditional 
companies do, and no single legacy lens has reliably measured whether a project is compounding durable advantage over time. The signals that 
matter are scattered across various onchain and oﬀchain metrics. Individually, they’re easy to cherry-pick or dismiss; collectively, they’ve lacked a 
consistent, transparent way to be weighed and compared. This proof-of-concept, which we’re calling the Disruption Factor (DF), attempts to solve 
that. 
Why We Built the DF 
Crypto doesn’t suﬀer from a lack of metrics; it suﬀers from a lack of synthesis. Adoption is multidimensional, spanning usage, integrations, 
economics, reliability, and mindshare, yet these signals are often trapped in separate silos that make conviction feel like guesswork for both 
enterprises and allocators. The Disruption Factor was built to ﬁx this, and to do so, it has four guiding principles: 
1. Transparency 
1. Every metric, weight, and transformation is fully open. No black-box scoring. No hidden levers. Analysts, institutions, and builders 
can audit, critique, or fully recreate the DF themselves. 
2. Customizability 
1. Diﬀerent stakeholders have diﬀerent evaluation criteria. Builders see the world diﬀerently from institutions. So the DF is modular; 
users can adjust pillar weights to satisfy their own needs and inputs based on their worldview. Messari provides a default version, but 
the framework is yours to reshape. 
3. Long-Term Thinking 
1. The DF prioritizes durable metrics through its seven pillars. Virality, noise, and speculative ﬂows matter, but they don’t dominate. 
4. Open-Source & Evolving 
1. Just like crypto, the DF is designed to evolve. Inspired by frameworks like ESG scores or credit ratings, it invites community input 
and improvement. As the industry matures, the scoring model will adapt alongside it. 
The Disruption Factor serves as a compass for durability, rather than a signal for short-term trades. Here’s how enterprises, allocators, and retail 
users can put it to work: 
● Enterprise Adopters: Use the DF to quickly benchmark L2s and identify which networks exhibit the most strength in your areas of interest, 
before committing engineering resources. It’s a practical starting map for chain selection and deeper diligence. 
● Investors/Fund Managers: Use the DF as a repeatable diligence layer to compare L2 networks on adoption quality, not just narrative 
strength. Because the pillars and weights are customizable, you can apply your own investment lens, whether you prioritize revenue 
durability, ecosystem depth, or enterprise traction, and see which projects rise under your thesis. 
               
 


---

## Page 304

303 
● Retail: Use the DF to zoom out and focus on networks building durable traction rather than short-term spikes in attention or incentives. It 
turns scattered fundamentals into a simple peer-relative score to support clearer long-term decisions. 
The Disruption Factor oﬀers a simple, intuitive framework that cuts through volatility and speculation to clearly identify which projects have made 
the most progress towards achieving a long-lasting fundamental impact in a given sector. In an environment where narratives move faster than 
fundamentals, the Disruption Factor helps us ask and quantify the question that really matters: 
Which projects are likely to drive lasting, fundamental progress over the long-term, and why? 
Methodology Overview 
The Disruption Factor measures how deeply a crypto project has embedded itself into the broader world and into mainstream user behavior. It 
evaluates not just onchain activity, but whether that activity is meaningfully replacing legacy systems, attracting non-crypto users, and turning into 
sticky, long-term adoption. 
To quantify this, we built a composite scoring model grounded in seven pillars: 
               
 


---

## Page 305

304 
 
Within each pillar, the DF evaluates multiple quantitative and qualitative metrics. To generate a single comparable score, we follow three steps: 
1. Normalize the data: Each metric is converted into a percentile rank (0–1) relative to sector peers. 
2. Adjust for gamability: Metrics that are easier to manipulate are discounted so they carry less inﬂuence. 
3. Weight and aggregate: Adjusted metrics are weighted, rolled up into pillar scores, and then summed into the ﬁnal DF score. 
Disruption Factor Formula: DF = Σ (Wi × Pi × (1 − Gi)) 
● Wi = weight of the metric 
● Pi = percentile rank (0-1) 
● Gi = gamability score (0-1) 
The DF score (0–100) benchmarks each project against its sector peers: 
● < 50 → Mostly crypto-native adoption; limited external embedment 
● 50–75 → Disruption is material; expanding beyond crypto-native users 
● > 75 → Infrastructure-grade, culturally sticky, systemically relevant 
               
 


---

## Page 306

305 
In this proof-of-concept, we scored thirteen L2s to debut the DF. We chose to begin with the L2 sector due to consistent onchain activity, clear 
competitive dynamics, and widely accessible metrics that make it an ideal proving ground for a standardized framework. Over time, we can 
expand the DF to other sectors, tailoring metrics and weights while maintaining the same core pillars. 
 
The results reveal a clear barbell in the L2 landscape: Arbitrum One (70) and Base (67) are pulling away as the leaders, with OP Mainnet (58) 
alone in the next tier. Below that, the ﬁeld compresses under 49, suggesting that many L2s remain early, sector-speciﬁc, or are still proving 
durability. The DF shifts the conversation from “who has the best narrative?” to “what are this chain’s current strengths or areas of opportunity?” – 
pinpointing the pillar gaps that separate tiers and making progress trackable as fundamentals improve. 
Arbitrum One 
               
 


---

## Page 307

306 
 
Arbitrum had the highest DF score of 69.5, leading in just 1/7 pillars, but was the runner-up in two others while ranking as the leader in 3/28 
individual metrics. Arbitrum’s lead is driven by durable DeFi economics, strong netﬂows, and ecosystem revenue, rather than a single breakout 
app, as evidenced by its leading position in the Economic Longevity pillar. Arbitrum has also been attracting a roster of enterprise builders 
(Robinhood, Franklin Templeton, and WisdomTree), reinforcing that its technology stack is viewed as a reliable base layer for production 
deployments. In DF terms, that combination, economic durability and credible adoption pathways, is exactly what separates a top-tier L2 from the 
long tail still proving staying power. 
Base

Base held the second-highest DF score of 67.1, leading in 4/7 pillars and ranking as the leader in 10/28 individual metrics. Base has a structural 
advantage that most L2s can’t replicate: a mainstream distribution channel (Coinbase). Coinbase converts awareness into users and users into 
sustained onchain activity, as evidenced by its leading position in the Usage Depth (Monthly Transactions, Chain Revenue, and Throughput), 
Sentiment & Narrative (Messari mindshare), and Project Stated Goal (DeFi TVL and Active Users) pillars. From the app thesis perspective, Base 
continues to be an oft-chosen chain to deploy on and houses notable DeFi and Consumer apps, such as Aerodrome and Zora. 
OP Mainnet

durable alignment and compounding ecosystem pull, reﬂected in its strength in the Network Eﬀects pillar. While the Optimism Superchain thesis 
is deﬁned by shared OP Stack standards and alignment across OP Chains, we score OP Mainnet on a standalone basis because the DF measures 
observable, chain-level durability today; any Superchain-wide upside should only lift OP Mainnet’s score once it shows up in OP Mainnet’s own 
usage, economics, and integrations.

Stablecoins Enter the Daily Lives of Billions 
Author: Ben O’Neil @ Bridge 
               
 


---

## Page 311

310 
 
Stablecoins became the topic dejure in 2025; every crypto company pivoted to them and every ﬁntech started building out a strategy of how they 
were going to adopt them. As a result, we saw traction and PMF in several important use cases, including remittances, corporate treasury, and 
stablecoin issuance. In 2026, the trees we planted will begin to bear fruit: we’ll see traditional ﬁntechs and payment companies start to build 
stablecoin products at scale, and stablecoins will begin to reach the everyday user. 
Remittances. Major platforms like Remitly, Zepz, Western Union, and Moneygram have come out publicly announcing their plans to integrate 
and adapt stablecoins into their platforms. As these products launch, we will see the impact on their business which will push every major 
remittance company to follow suit. By the end of 2026, stablecoins will be the underlying infrastructure of global payments. 
Corporate Treasury. On a larger scale, businesses have begun to adopt stablecoins to move funds between global partners and entities faster and 
cheaper than ever before. Multinationals such as Starlink and Stripe are already moving millions of dollars a day via stablecoins and companies 
such as Beam (Modern Treasury) and Rail (Ripple) are being acquired to expedite product adoption. Public data will show B2B and treasury 
payments reaching into the hundreds of billions in volume in 2026. 
Stablecoin issuance. After growing 50% YoY in 2025, stablecoin supply will 2x in 2026 to over $600 billion in AUM. The majority of the 
increase in supply will come from platform-speciﬁc stablecoins such as USDH, CASH, and PYUSD compared to general purpose stablecoins. 
The distribution of market cap will continue to democratize with newer players eating into market share. The majority of enterprises that launch a 
new stablecoin product will also issue their own stablecoin on platforms such as Bridge and Anchorage. 
While many may think of 2025 as the year of the Stablecoin, 2026 is when they truly get put into the hands of users and enter the daily life of 
billions of people globally. 
Morpho Grows its Lending Market Share 
Author: Toe Bautista @ GSR 
 
Aave’s liquidity, brand, and process power remain among the most underappreciated moats in crypto. It exhibits power-law dynamics across 
nearly every dimension: ~98% of collateral is BTC, ETH, or stablecoins; 80–85% of revenues come from interest income; and ~80% of activity 
remains on Ethereum. As such, ETH and BTC market cap are the primary drivers of Aave’s market share. This is a feature and a bug. In bull 
markets, when BTC and ETH appreciate, Aave’s outstanding borrows tend to increase as users seek leverage. However, Aave’s overreliance on 
speculation causes activity to compress in bear cycles when price unwinds. While eﬀective in the current paradigm, Aave remains beholden to the 
growth of those existing assets and is unlikely to support more complex collateral types, such as equities or tokenized RWAs. 
               
 


---

## Page 312

311 
 
Conversely, Morpho’s trajectory has meaningfully diverged. As of Jan 2024, both Aave and Morpho’s borrow activity had a 0.8–0.9 correlation 
with ETH’s price. Morpho’s correlation has since dropped to 0.4 while net borrows grew >400%. For BTC price, Aave borrows have a 0.8 
correlation, compared to 0.4 for Morpho. 
This illustrates why Morpho is well-positioned to gain market share: it enables product diversiﬁcation and broader user behavior independent of 
speculative cycles. In contrast, the inability to oﬀer ﬁxed-rate products constrains Aave’s borrow-side TAM, especially for RWAs. Institutions are 
disincentivized to use Aave when they must continually requote positions as variable rates move. Morpho V2 solves this through ﬁxed-rate, 
cross-margin loans. Given the clear demand for ﬁxed-rate exposure (see: Pendle’s $40 million in 2025 revenue), Morpho’s modular architecture is 
better suited for exogenous collateral while isolating risk across collateral types. 
As corporates and ﬁntechs expand their onchain presence, Morpho is architecturally better positioned than Aave to capture this wave. In fact, 
Morpho partnered with Coinbase and Revolut; Aave acquired Strobe Finance, emphasizing both the market’s preference for modular money 
markets and the widening divergence in GTM. Finally, Aave’s limited product optionality and reliance on ETH-driven speculation weaken its 
moat. By contrast, Morpho’s strategic partnerships and modular design set it up to meaningfully grow lending market share in 2026, ultimately 
               
 


---

## Page 313

312 
fracturing Aave’s long-standing network eﬀects. 
Investing in a Meme World 
Author: Kunal Goel @ LayerZero 
One for the Memes 
Memecoins have won. They have succeeded in capturing the speculative premium in crypto. In earlier cycles, crypto’s speculative fervor was 
focused on altcoins, which mostly served as attention coins for their sectors. A particularly notable example was the repricing of metaverse tokens 
after Facebook rebranded to Meta in October 2021. 
 
This kind of speculative price action now happens mostly in memecoins, and less so in alts. The eﬀect of this shift is clear in a prescient post by 
               
 


---

## Page 314

313 
memecoin proponent Murad. 
 
The Post-Memecoin Era 
The performance of most alts in 2025 suggests that Murad was right: memecoins now capture most speculative demand. This, however, creates an 
opportunity: the altcoin sector now trades much closer to its fundamental value. Altcoins with improving fundamentals in such a market are 
especially attractive, particularly where they have been written oﬀ by market participants and have become contrarian. 
Through that lens, I’ll evaluate the fundamentals of LayerZero, the project I know best. The same framework can be used to identify and evaluate 
other projects in the post-memecoin era. 
Winning Category 
LayerZero was created for a multichain future, a thesis that is rapidly playing out. 2025 saw new chain announcements and launches from large 
               
 


---

## Page 315

314 
crypto and traditional companies including Stripe, Circle, Tether, Monad, MegaETH, and more. As crypto becomes more mainstream, a growing 
multichain ecosystem will further increase demand for interoperability. 
Category Winner 
LayerZero dominates interoperability across every metric. In 2025, LayerZero had ~65% market share in crosschain messages and ~80% market 
share in crosschain volume among general messaging protocols (excluding Circle’s CCTP). LayerZero’s dominance stems from supporting a large 
number of high-quality chains and assets. 
Growing PMF 
LayerZero has found strong product-market ﬁt in interoperable stablecoins. LayerZero supports more than 60% of all stablecoins in crypto, 
including USDT through its Legacy Mesh, USDT0, Ethena’s USDe, PayPal’s PYUSD, Wyoming’s FRNT, and more. LayerZero also supports 
other major crypto assets such as WBTC, WETH, EtherFi’s weETH, and XAUT0. 
Value Capture and Buybacks 
LayerZero acquired Stargate and launched a swaps product in Q3 2025. Verticalizing through Stargate allows LayerZero to build a 
consumer-facing product and directly capture value. All proﬁts from Stargate products directly support ZRO buybacks. 
Additionally, LayerZero Foundation and LayerZero Labs conducted large discretionary buybacks in H2 2025. In the future, the protocol’s fee 
switch can be turned on to programmatically buy back ZRO. Cumulatively, LayerZero executed among the largest buybacks of any crypto project 
in 2025. 
Looking Forward 
Murad was right: memecoins have won. But that victory creates opportunity in places where market participants are no longer paying attention. In 
my view, LayerZero is one of those opportunities.

2026 is Shaping up to be the Year of (Equity) Perps 
Author: Sunny Shi @ Syncracy Capital 
 
The relationship between traditional ﬁnance and crypto has matured greatly in 2026. This year, we saw worlds collide, with Wall Street 
experimenting with crypto IPOs and DATs while onchain participants opened the ﬂoodgates to mass stablecoin and RWA adoption. This period of 
interchange has revived TradFi interest in crypto concepts, while crypto natives increasingly recognize that RWAs are a path towards bringing 
higher quality modes of ﬁnance and speculation onchain. 
Perp DEXs are relatively underdiscussed by TradFi outlets yet are a clear beneﬁciary of this cross-pollination. For example, equity perps import 
RWAs onchain in a format that is appealing to crypto natives, while exporting our crypto rails to new traders who now have permissionless access 
to highly levered stock and commodity futures. The underlying innovations that perp DEXs bring to the table are vast. These are fully solvent and 
transparent onchain order books that could allow anyone in the world to speculate on assets at previously unimaginable levels of leverage. 
Perps are: 
● More capital eﬃcient than traditional levered margin products 
● More digestible for retail given their simplicity 
● More eﬀective for certain trades when compared to options 
● Better for market participation if 24/7 trading is unlocked 
A South Korean trader on Hyperliquid can now place a 10x levered GOOGL long Saturday night without worrying about expiry, decay, and 
convexity. Astoundingly, they can do this without relying on a traditional brokerage account. 
Furthermore, DEXs may get a head start on equity perps simply because they can move faster and build natively around the mechanics that perps 
require (real-time margining, instant liquidations, and vertical integration). Centralized exchanges, especially those tied to TradFi frameworks, 
face slower product approval cycles, legacy clearing models, and stricter regulatory boundaries that limit how quickly they can introduce new 
derivatives formats. By contrast, DEXs can iterate openly onchain, experiment rapidly, and launch globally under the current regulatory regime 
that has been relatively hands-oﬀ. This agility gives them a natural advantage in shaping the earliest and most compelling versions of equity perps. 
In less than two months, Hyperliquid has already surpassed $5 billion in cumulative trading volumes on their HIP-3 products. Perhaps, this is the 
unlock we need to push the DEX:CEX ratio higher in the futures category. 
To conclude, it is entertaining to watch crypto pundits complain about the lack of innovation within the arena, while tokenization, stablecoins and

prediction markets have become the talk of the town amongst external investors. These aforementioned narratives existed in prior cycles, but even 
in the mania of 2021, few predicted they would evolve into the global phenomena that they are today. My view is that the perps phenomenon is 
coming into form onchain right now, with an opportunity set that is just as expansive waiting to be realized and recognized. I believe that 
in 2026, equity perps will onboard new users onchain and attract growing exogenous investment appetite for crypto narratives. It is highly possible 
that equity perps develop into crypto’s newest killer use case while also becoming TradFi’s new crypto ﬁxation. 
Pricing TGEs with Prediction Markets 
Author: Amir @ Keyrock 
 
In 2026, Prediction Markets will operate as a direct market for future outcomes that institutions and users rely on to price risk, hedge 
uncertainty, and act on information in real time. 
For institutions and retail users, prediction markets represent the simplest form of derivatives. They function as binary contracts with ﬁxed 
payouts and capped risk, without the structural complexity of traditional instruments. They remove the need for volatility assumptions, 
discounting models, margin, time decay, and strike selection. As a result, they are uniquely suited for hedging discrete events such as earnings, 
product launches, and macro releases, without exposure to implied volatility crush. 
More importantly, prediction markets allow participants to hedge the event itself rather than its ﬁnancial proxy. Instead of expressing macro 
risk through equities, FX, or volatility indices, institutions can hedge elections, policy shifts, wars, inﬂation regimes, and regulatory outcomes 
directly. As these markets deepen, their pricing increasingly mirrors institutional pricing and establishes prediction markets as leading 
indicators of macro stress and regime shifts. 
They also unlock entirely new hedging surfaces. Through pre-IPO and pre-TGE markets, investors gain the ﬁrst scalable way to hedge 
private-market risk at scale, a market that remains largely unexplored and spans hundreds of billions in value. Valuations that once appeared 
only on listing day become tradeable probability curves months or years in advance, turning opaque moments into continuously priced 
distributions across multiple strikes. 
Instead of discovering token valuations in a single chaotic listing moment, prediction markets allow TGEs to be priced in advance through a 
market-driven valuation curve. Funds, teams, and protocol contributors submit valuation levels they are willing to trade, while market makers 
aggregate that order ﬂow into structured FDV pricing lines listed as tradable event contracts. 
Once live, this structure creates a public, continuous probability distribution for a token’s future valuation. Teams and early investors can 
hedge without touching the cap table, retail gains synthetic access to pre-TGE risk, and the market itself forms a real-time forward curve for FDV. 
Instead of relying on private rounds or narrative anchoring, token launches become pre-priced, hedgeable ﬁnancial events.As direct event risk 
moves away from proxies, institutions and protocols will begin using prediction markets to hedge real exposure. That shift is what excites me 
               
 


---

## Page 318

317 
most. 
All Roads Lead to the Wallet 
Author: Justin Baba 
 
Society continues to drift toward higher-risk, gambling-like behavior, and crypto is positioned to capture this ﬂow through products that traditional 
markets do not oﬀer. In 2026, two ﬁnancial instruments should beneﬁt most from this shift: perpetual futures and prediction markets. But the 
largest beneﬁciary will ultimately be the wallets that sit above them. 
Perpetual exchanges once focused exclusively on crypto assets, but upgrades such as Hyperliquid’s HIP-3 now enable permissionless listing of 
perpetual markets for non-crypto categories, including equities. As these capabilities expand, teams will experiment with increasingly niche 
products, such as Pokemon card indices, collectibles, and other long-tail assets. Meanwhile, perpetuals tied to RWAs or commodities allow traders 
to generate higher returns from traditionally lower-volatility assets. If liquidity forms around these instruments, perpetuals could become a 
standard way for investors to express cross-asset theses. 
Prediction markets push this trend further. Platforms like Polymarket and Kalshi have scaled meaningfully over the past year, but the next stage 
will involve leverage, combinatorial trades (parlays), and richer payoﬀ structures. These features will draw in new capital from risk-seeking 
participants, such as sports betters and sophisticated forecasters. Over time, these enhancements will likely be built on top of or integrated directly 
into existing prediction market platforms. 
Although these exchanges supply the underlying infrastructure, the real winner in this landscape is the wallet. Perpetual exchanges and prediction 
market platforms will compete with each other by lowering fees and deepening liquidity, but wallets can aggregate across them, surfacing the best 
execution for the end-user. This is the essence of the Fat Wallet Thesis. 
Distribution, one of the hardest problems in crypto, is far less of a constraint for wallets, since they are one of the ﬁrst interfaces new participants 
create. If a wallet can provide seamless access to trading, swapping, forecasting, and cash conversion within a single application, users have little 
incentive to leave. This positions the wallet as the primary consumer-facing interface for all of the user’s activities. Phantom already demonstrates 
this dynamic: traders can access Hyperliquid’s equity perpetuals, swap via Jupiter, and convert assets to cash without leaving the app or 
understanding which protocol they are interacting with. 
Looking ahead to 2026, wallets will continue adding features that abstract away the underlying protocols. This is only the beginning. Over time, 
wallets may integrate traditional ﬁnance tools as well, becoming the consolidated home for a majority of an individual’s ﬁnancial activity. 
Rise of the Crypto Yield Engineer 
Author: Micah Casella @ Hypersphere 
               
 


---

## Page 319

318 
How Being Delta-Neutral on Aerodrome Delivers 20–40% APR — and Why 2026 Belongs to Protocol Cash Flows 
- 
Somewhere. Out there. In the deepest corner of the bear market, a fund with a comfortable eight ﬁgures of AUM hasn’t lost its appetite for risk. 
This fund just wants 20% annual returns and is willing to dance at the edge of the risk curve to ﬁnd it. But it doesn’t play the ticker game — it 
specializes in yields. And, so, it sets out on a hunt for creativity in the market. 
Enter the delta-neutral Aerodrome trader. The yield-seeking fund hires a sleuth who discovers a seven-ﬁgure portfolio of veAERO, quietly 
collecting 31% APR weekly, with all gains converted to and held in USDC. 
At ﬁrst the fund assumes the trader is running a naked long AERO bet. Then the sleuth uncovers a perpetual short position on Hyperliquid under 
the same wallet address matching the size of the trader’s locked AERO. With funding rates running positive, the trader is earning roughly 11% 
annualized funding income — on top of the 31% APR from fees and bribes (the yield sources on Aerodrome). 
This isn’t speculation. It’s synthetic yield engineering. Across mid-sized funds in 2026, the hunt is on — not for price, but for protocol cash ﬂows. 
And crypto is notorious for seeding quick, high cash ﬂow platforms. Aerodrome’s veAERO isn’t a token play. It’s a yield machine that can be 
delta-hedged. “Smart capital” is sick of chopping themselves up on volatility and chasing narratives. They’ll lock, short, and harvest. 
Many funds (and retail) bled out in 2025 chasing momentum or picking the wrong tickers. The funds looking to learn something are realizing that 
they could have been pulling in 20-40% yields as active participants of various crypto protocols instead of losing over a quarter of their book 
while speculating on Binance. 
It’s true that synthetic yield engineering is not risk-free. The major operational risk lies in Gamma PnL — the cost incurred from dynamically 
rebalancing the perp short as the underlying (e.g., AERO) price moves, especially during rapid, volatile spikes. Furthermore, the single-most 
threatening variable is a sustained ﬂip to negative funding, where the cost of maintaining the short position outweighs the income from fees and 
bribes, eﬀectively making the hedge a cost rather than an additional source of yield. 
Regardless, the trade-oﬀ is calculated and the risk is operational (cost of hedging, basis risk) rather than based on directional price movements. 
This is the fundamental, structural advantage. It allows the creative asset manager to isolate and capture the high cash ﬂows inherent in crypto 
protocols while sidelining the volatility that most folks are unprepared to handle. 
So what’s the 2026 thesis again? 
That crypto funds and retail investors will ﬁnd more alpha in savvy risk management over asset selection. Our industry produces the fastest 
$100+ million revenue companies and will continue to grind out more opportunities where fees are captured. Picking tickers is a crowded and 
often rigged game. The skillset of the next cycle will favor creativity over gambling, valuing those that can build new delta-neutral yield strategies 
that scale to seven or eight ﬁgures and reliably harvest DeFi cash ﬂows. 
P.S. 
I’ll be posting a slightly more detailed follow-up of the AERO strategy on X.

Crypto Sentiment Will Improve 
Author: Nick Garcia @ Breed 
 
The crypto economy entered 2025 with sentiment at all-time highs: BTC was on the verge of breaking the six-ﬁgure level, Darth Gensler was 
gone, and the dawn of the crypto capital of the world was approaching. Fast forward to EOY, and sentiment is at all-time lows despite getting 
everything we wanted from regulators. So where does that take us in 2026? 
First, token holder protections will be top of mind. Gone are the days when token holders will accept being the funders of the Bali slow rug. The 
medicine thus far has been MetaDAO ownership coins, but expect new models to emerge. 
Second, crypto-native protocols will accelerate their adoption of and interoperability with equities. Hyperliquid is the clear early winner with 
equity perps, but expect new projects to follow suit and DeFi adoption emerge. 
Third, the stablecoin duopoly will further erode and more major protocols will launch native stablecoins to capture the yield. USDH was the 
canary in the coal mine, and Ethena’s Stablecoin-as-a-Service provides the infrastructure for projects to launch their own native stablecoins, with 
Sui, MegaETH, and Jupiter as the ﬁrst customers. 
Lastly, crypto sentiment will improve. If you are a multicycle-surviving cockroach or divinely protected individual still here, you are not going 
anywhere. However, collectively we must avoid succumbing to the prisoner’s dilemma and recognize that things need to change in 2026. I believe 
the market has shown its hand post-10/10 as to what that will entail. 
Crypto’s Transition from Asset Class to Tech Sector 
Author: Maartje Bus @ The Medici Network 
 
For years we’ve treated crypto as a single asset class because that’s exactly how it behaved. Now, that label has become misleading. 
The Great Decoupling 
Crypto is increasingly shedding the “asset class” label because its components no longer move together or share a common risk-return proﬁle – 
the deﬁning requirement of an asset class in the ﬁrst place. Bitcoin now behaves more like a macro store of value: volatility has structurally 
declined, institutional participation has deepened, and its price action is increasingly decoupled from the rest of crypto. Ethereum and major 
L1/L2 ecosystems, by contrast, trade more like high-growth technology infrastructure, with performance tied to adoption, fee generation, and 
application-level activity rather than broad market sentiment. 
               
 


---

## Page 321

320 
Infrastructure Over Ideology 
Beyond market behavior, this divergence reﬂects a deeper structural shift. Blockchains and core crypto primitives are increasingly understood not 
as ideological alternatives to existing systems, but as infrastructure for re-platforming ﬁnancial services and enabling new digital primitives more 
broadly. The early emphasis on decentralization as an end in itself is giving way to a more pragmatic focus on utility, reliability, and integration. 
Stablecoins are the clearest expression of this shift: widely used, tightly integrated into existing ﬁnancial ﬂows, and largely abstracted away from 
the end user. Increasingly, crypto-native primitives – including lending, settlement, and liquidity – are embedded “under the hood” of centralized 
or regulated applications rather than surfaced as standalone decentralized products. 
Crypto as a Tech Sector 
Bitcoin aside – now eﬀectively a category of its own – this evolution makes the rest of crypto look less like an asset class and more like a 
technology sector, both economically and from an investment perspective – much like the internet. What ties these components together is not 
shared price behavior, but shared infrastructure including blockchains, wallets, middleware, and DeFi primitives. Value creation and investment 
exposure are therefore distributed across multiple layers and can be expressed through a mix of tokens, public equities, derivatives, credit, and 
structured vehicles rather than a single, monolithic trade. 
Looking Forward 
This transition is likely to accelerate through 2026. Blockchain infrastructure is increasingly embedded in real-world ﬁnancial applications rather 
than standalone decentralized products, with stablecoins leading, and payments, lending, and settlement following close behind. Tokenization will 
continue to bring traditional assets onchain, blurring asset-class boundaries in general. A growing pipeline of crypto-native IPOs will expand the 
investable universe, while ﬁnancial “super apps” – combining cross-asset brokerage, payments, credit and other services in a single interface – are 
beginning to take shape, powered by digital wallets and blockchain rails. 
As crypto continues to mature into foundational ﬁnancial infrastructure, many of the characteristics that once deﬁned it will begin to lose their 
centrality – meme-driven discourse, ideology-ﬁrst application design, and synchronized boom-bust cycles. Capital and development will 
increasingly concentrate around economically legible products that deliver clear user value, rather than applications built primarily to be 
decentralized or tokenized for their own sake. 
Parting Thoughts 
This shift matters because it fundamentally reframes what adoption means. Crypto adoption no longer depends on users buying tokens or 
consciously “using crypto,” but on blockchain infrastructure serving as the anchoring layer for value – powering stablecoins today and an 
               
 


---

## Page 322

321 
expanding set of tokenized assets over time. While these assets increasingly live onchain, access and interaction are abstracted through wallets and 
platforms that conceal blockchain complexity. As a result, onchain activity and economic relevance can accelerate even as crypto recedes from 
view – reﬂecting its evolution from a traded asset class into a technology sector. 
Bitcoin vs. Altcoins 
Author: Tulip King @ CounterParty TV 
 
I think moving into 2026 we'll continue to see bifurcation between Bitcoin and the rest of the crypto market. That’s not to say Bitcoin and 
Altcoins can’t go up or down at the same time, but rather they’ll be doing so for entirely independent reasons. The days of altcoins working like 
“bitcoin-beta” are dead, they were killed in 2025, and they’re not coming back. That means you need to have a framework for both Bitcoin and 
Altcoins looking forward if your aim is to maximize opportunity. 
With respect to Bitcoin: The game is the same it’s always been, money. Make no mistake Bitcoin is in a death match against gold and the dollar. 
Counter-intuitively, I think Bitcoin’s appreciation looking forward will be correlated with the total stablecoin supply (check out Messari’s data for 
this). The more stablecoins we get and the faster, the more Bitcoin should appreciate. If stablecoin supply continues to increment at a glacial pace, 
it’ll be a while before Bitcoin makes any impressive moves. 
This is because we need to drown out all the ﬁlth in crypto that isn’t Money, speciﬁcally the L1 tokens that have been allowed to LARP as money 
for far too long… Yes that means ETH, BNB, SOL, ADA, XRP, you name it — are all going to need to come down to reasonable multiples based 
on fees/net-inﬂation (read: price must come down). The rapid adoption of stablecoins has two cleansing aﬀects: 
1. We can stop pretending these L1 tokens are money 
2. I expect surplus digital dollars to ﬂow into Bitcoin the same way we’ve seen surplus physical dollars ﬂow into gold. 
With respect to Altcoins: I don’t have much to say other than we’re in the “Amazon Bottom” of crypto’s dotcom crash (the ’21 DeFi Summer 
cycle). It’s not going to be easy but for the ﬁrst time I believe there are investable projects that will outperform Bitcoin on a multi-cycle horizon, 
which is something we’ve never really seen before. Just be careful, I believe the projects are going to break the mold of DeFi/L1 slop and come 
from entirely unexpected places. There’s still a lot of falling knives just waiting for people to catch them. 
Crypto AI Becomes Competitive

2026 is the year crypto-AI stops being discussed as a moral upgrade and starts being adopted as a competitive one. Founders will increasingly 
recognize that cryptoeconomic protocols let them build AI startups that outperform traditional ones. Not because they’re fairer, but because they

## Page 323

322 
coordinate people, capital, and compute at a speed and scale legacy structures can’t match. The network where most of this experimentation is 
already happening is Bittensor, and in 2026, it will continue to pull away as it attracts the strongest founders. 
The Capitalization of Experience 
Author: Brody Adreon 
Introduction 
To understand where Crypto AI is headed, we must ﬁrst acknowledge where it has failed. 
The initial promise of Crypto AI, the "Airbnb for GPUs," was a brilliant narrative that attempted to address the compute bottlenecks of a 
production-constrained TSMC. As a result, our CT echo chamber parroted decentralized GPU marketplaces such as Nosana, Akash, and Render 
as hyperscaler alternatives, and the industry’s saving grace. 
In reality, these protocols failed to address the latency and orchestration bottlenecks that hyperscalers solve through physical GPU co-location. 
Lacking the synchronicity required for foundational model training, decentralized aggregators were relegated to niche inference workloads. 
Then came the "Agent Meta" of Q4 2024 and Q1 2025. This was the vertical’s most recent ﬂash of excitement, but looking back, these tokens 
were repackaged memecoins masquerading as innovation. They had personality and were fun to interact with, but failed to spawn any real 
economic value, ultimately turning into yet another PvP trading meta. 
Crypto AI has undergone several iterations and much experimentation, but the main problem has been its inability to ﬁnd PMF within the AI 
community and end consumer market. However, a new area of model research has emerged this year that aims to drive value to the researchers 
who leverage it so they can, in turn, produce more performant models and agents for the end consumer: Tokenized Reinforcement Learning 
(RL) Environments. 
My prediction posits that the next great tokenized asset class lies not at the infrastructure or application layer, but in the Experience Layer. This 
new vertical represents a multi-billion dollar opportunity to ﬁnancialize the "long tail" of human experience and nuance, creating a permissionless 
marketplace for the specialized training environments that centralized frontier labs cannot scale independently. 
               
 


---

## Page 324

323 
 
From Static Datasets to Dynamic Gyms 
The bottleneck for increasingly useful AI is no longer “intelligence” or reasoning capabilities, but rather “experience" and functional dynamism. 
Historically, developers attempted to bridge this gap with Supervised Fine-Tuning (SFT): feeding models static datasets of expert demonstrations. 
While SFT allows a model to imitate a correct answer, it never forces the model to internalize the reasoning required to reach it. 
For example, if you want a "Traﬃc Law Agent," ﬁne-tuning it on a static database of legal codes is insuﬃcient. The agent might know the law, but 
it doesn't know how to navigate the chaotic, edge-case-ﬁlled reality of a contested ticket in a municipal court. 
This is where Reinforcement Learning (RL) replaces static tuning. In RL, agents are not taught, they are raised. They act within a dynamic 
environment, receiving rewards for correct clerical work and penalties for errors. They develop heuristics through millions of simulated 
interactions. 
In 2026, the competitive advantage belongs to whoever owns and contributes to the most robust, complex, and edge-case-rich Environment. 
               
 


---

## Page 325

324 
The Environment is the Asset 
Projects such as Prime Intellect, Nous Research, and Aﬃne are working to decouple these environments from the models, transforming static 
datasets and post-training methodologies into permissionless & adversarial environments that ﬁnancialize the learning process and reward all 
stakeholders. 
Consider the Traﬃc Law example: Instead of a centralized company building a simulation, a protocol opens a "Traﬃc Gym" to the world where 
participants earn a stake in the network by actively contributing to the gym's complexity and accuracy. 
● Data Contributor: A user in Austin captures and uploads dashcam footage of a roundabout, a confusing (depends on who you ask) road 
layout where standard self-driving models consistently crash or freeze. 
● Logic Contributor: A law student encodes the speciﬁc local ordinance for that roundabout into the environment, deﬁning the strict 
"ground truth" for who actually has the right of way in that edge case. 
● Validator: A veriﬁed human reviewer grades the agent’s attempt to navigate this new scenario, providing the ﬁnal "reward signal" 
(pass/fail) that updates the model’s weights. 
These participants are capitalizing the environment by systematically closing the gap between general intelligence and speciﬁc reality. They 
identiﬁed the blind spot (the complex roundabout), codiﬁed the rules (the ordinance), and validated the solution (the review). 
As this cycle repeats, the environment transforms from a passive simulation into a productive capital asset: a proprietary, localized compliance 
layer that generates royalties from every autonomous ﬂeet or insurance model that must access this validated ground truth to prevent costly 
accidents or settle liability claims. 
The Value Architecture 
This new asset class functions less like a commodity and more like royalty-bearing IP, shifting the investment thesis from capturing the ﬂeeting 
value of individual, ephemeral agents to owning the dynamic, evolving environments from which inﬁnite agents spawn. 
The value ﬂows through three distinct streams: 
● Access Rent (Training Revenue): Developers must pay to validate their agents against high-ﬁdelity edge cases. Protocols like Aﬃne and 
Prime Intellect have operationalized this mechanism: users pay to access the network's intelligence, and that revenue is programmatically 
distributed to the contributors who provided the resources and expertise. 
● Performance Royalties (Agent Value Capture): This is the moonshot. As envisioned in Symbolic Capital’s "World's RL Gym" thesis, 
the Environment is the ultimate constraint on intelligence. By combining this with Prime Intellect’s "model ownership" primitives, smart 
contracts can enforce a fee switch on an agent's future utility, returning a portion of its revenue to the environment that trained it. 
● Standardization Premium: Investors speculate on which speciﬁc environments become the essential "courseware" for a vertical. Nous 
Research is facilitating this via Atropos, their open-source RL framework. Rather than a single "Global Standard," Atropos enables a 
               
 


---

## Page 326

325 
composable market of thousands of specialized, immutable "ground truth" environments. Models are rigorously validated against this 
diverse suite of stress tests, accruing value to the speciﬁc environments that provide the necessary nuance to certify an agent as an expert. 
Applying this to our Traﬃc Agent example, the economic cycle is complete: The ﬂeet operator pays rent to the network to train on the "Austin 
Roundabout" edge case, the agent pays royalties back to the stakers from the revenue it earns settling insurance claims; and the Environment 
token itself accrues a premium as it establishes itself as the only veriﬁed standard for Austin municipal traﬃc law. 
Conclusion 
If 2025 was deﬁned by the commoditization of intelligence, 2026 will be deﬁned by the capitalization of experience. 
The community has pivoted from competing on hardware to unlocking its true wedge: coordination. Tokenized RL Environments empower the 
open-source community to curate a library of skill too complex, localized, and dynamic for any single corporation to replicate. 
This is Crypto AI’s ultimate promise and original intention: using distributed incentives to turn human nuance and experience into the scarcest 
asset in the machine economy.
